 We owe you an explanation. 

December 5: An important update for readers in the United States. 

Please don't skip this 1-minute read. It's Friday, December 5, and this moment matters for Wikipedia because we haven't hit our goal yet. If you're like us, you've used Wikipedia countless times. To settle an argument with a friend. To satisfy a curiosity. Whether it's 3 in the morning or afternoon, Wikipedia is useful in your life. Please give $2.75.

After nearly 25 years, Wikipedia is still the internet we were promisedâ€”created by people, not by machines. It's not perfect, but it's not here to push a point of view. It's owned by a nonprofit, not a giant technology company or a billionaire.

Just 2% of our readers donate, so if you have given in the past and Wikipedia still provides you with $2.75 worth of knowledge, donate today. If you are undecided, remember any contribution helps.

25 years of the internet at its **best**

Where your donation goes

 Accountability and transparency are core values at the Wikimedia Foundation. We manage funds and resources to ensure that every contribution supports our mission. We have earned the Platinum Seal of Transparency from Candid (formerly GuideStar), and Charity Navigator awarded us its highest rating. You can [read our most recent annual report](https://annual.wikimedia.org/) for more information about our financial health. 

 Investment in Technology 45%
Nearly half of our budget goes toward supporting the technology that powers Wikipedia and other Wikimedia projects. We are constantly working to enhance the user experience for both contributors and readers, improve site security, and ensure reliable access to our websites globally. This infrastructure and product support sustain one of the top ten most visited websites in the world, all at a fraction of the cost of popular for-profit websites.

 Support for Volunteers 34%
The global reach of Wikimedia projects is made possible by the hard work of volunteers from across the globe. We provide grants, legal support, and other resources to help build vibrant volunteer communities. Additionally, we promote community engagement through outreach initiatives and advocate for the growth and protection of free knowledge.

 General and Administrative Expenses 12%
Operational costs are essential for the smooth management and governance of the Wikimedia Foundation. These expenses help us recruit top talent and support staff around the world, empowering them to carry out the mission of the Wikimedia Foundation.

 Allocation to Fundraising Efforts 11%
Donor support is crucial to sustaining Wikipedia and our other free knowledge endeavors. Our team is committed to efficient and effective fundraising throughout the year, ensuring that every contribution helps advance our mission.

The **United States of America** (**USA**), also known as the **United States** (**U.S.**) or **America**, is a country primarily located in [North America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_America "North America"). It is a [federal republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_republic "Federal republic") of 50 [states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._state "U.S. state") and a [federal capital district](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capital_districts_and_territories "Capital districts and territories"), [Washington, D.C.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington,_D.C. "Washington, D.C.") The 48 [contiguous states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contiguous_states "Contiguous states") border [Canada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canada "Canada") to the north and [Mexico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexico "Mexico") to the south, with the [semi-exclave](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semi-exclave "Semi-exclave") of [Alaska](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alaska "Alaska") in the northwest and the [archipelago](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archipelago "Archipelago") of [Hawaii](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hawaii "Hawaii") in the [Pacific Ocean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pacific_Ocean "Pacific Ocean"). The United States also asserts sovereignty over five [major island territories](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States "Territories of the United States") and [various uninhabited islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Minor_Outlying_Islands "United States Minor Outlying Islands") in [Oceania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oceania "Oceania") and the [Caribbean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caribbean "Caribbean").[[j]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-29) It is a [megadiverse country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Megadiverse_country "Megadiverse country"), with the world's [third-largest land area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area "List of countries and dependencies by area")[[c]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-largestcountry-15) and [third-largest population](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population "List of countries and dependencies by population"), exceeding 340 million.[[k]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-pop_clock-32)

[Paleo-Indians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paleo-Indians "Paleo-Indians") first migrated from North Asia to North America over 12,000 years ago, and formed various civilizations. [Spanish colonization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas "Spanish colonization of the Americas") established [Spanish Florida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Florida "Spanish Florida") in 1513, the first European colony in what is now the continental United States. [British colonization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_colonization_of_the_Americas "British colonization of the Americas") followed with the 1607 settlement of [Virginia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colony_of_Virginia "Colony of Virginia"), the first of the [Thirteen Colonies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies "Thirteen Colonies"). [Enslavement of Africans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slavery_in_the_colonial_history_of_the_United_States "Slavery in the colonial history of the United States") was practiced in all colonies by 1770 and supplied most of the labor for the [Southern Colonies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Colonies "Southern Colonies")' [plantation economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plantation_economy "Plantation economy"). Clashes with the [British Crown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Crown "The Crown") over taxation and lack of [parliamentary representation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/No_taxation_without_representation "No taxation without representation") sparked the [American Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Revolution "American Revolution"), leading to the [Declaration of Independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence "United States Declaration of Independence") on July 4, 1776. Victory in the 1775â€“1783 [Revolutionary War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War "American Revolutionary War") brought international recognition of U.S. sovereignty and fueled [westward expansion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Territorial_evolution_of_the_United_States "Territorial evolution of the United States"), dispossessing [native inhabitants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States "Native Americans in the United States"). As more states [were admitted](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Admission_to_the_Union "Admission to the Union"), a Northâ€“South [division over slavery](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slave_states_and_free_states "Slave states and free states") led the [Confederate States of America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America "Confederate States of America") to attempt secession and fight [the Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War) "Union (American Civil War)") in the 1861â€“1865 [American Civil War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Civil_War "American Civil War"). With the United States' victory and reunification, [slavery was abolished nationally](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thirteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution "Thirteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution"). By 1900, the country had established itself as a [great power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_power "Great power"), a status solidified after its involvement in [World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I "World War I"). Following [Japan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empire_of_Japan "Empire of Japan")'s [attack on Pearl Harbor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor "Attack on Pearl Harbor") in 1941, the U.S. [entered World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_entry_into_World_War_II "American entry into World War II"). [Its aftermath](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aftermath_of_World_War_II "Aftermath of World War II") left the U.S. and the [Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union") as rival [superpowers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superpower "Superpower"), competing for [ideological dominance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ideological_dominance "Ideological dominance") and [international influence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_influence "International influence") during the [Cold War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War "Cold War"). The [Soviet Union's collapse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union "Dissolution of the Soviet Union") in 1991 ended the Cold War, leaving the U.S. as the world's sole superpower.

The [U.S. national government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States "Federal government of the United States") is a [presidential](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidential_system "Presidential system") constitutional federal republic and [representative democracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Representative_democracy "Representative democracy") with [three separate branches](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Separation_of_powers_under_the_United_States_Constitution "Separation of powers under the United States Constitution"): [legislative](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Congress "United States Congress"), [executive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_federal_executive_departments "United States federal executive departments"), and [judicial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_judiciary_of_the_United_States "Federal judiciary of the United States"). It has a [bicameral](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bicameralism "Bicameralism") national legislature composed of the [House of Representatives](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives "United States House of Representatives") (a [lower house](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lower_house "Lower house") based on population) and the [Senate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Senate "United States Senate") (an [upper house](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Upper_house "Upper house") based on equal representation for each state). [Federalism grants substantial autonomy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federalism_in_the_United_States "Federalism in the United States") to the 50 states. In addition, 574 Native American tribes have [sovereignty rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tribal_sovereignty_in_the_United_States "Tribal sovereignty in the United States"), and there are 326 [Native American reservations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Native_American_reservations "Native American reservations"). Since the 1850s, the [Democratic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States) "Democratic Party (United States)") and [Republican](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States) "Republican Party (United States)") parties have dominated [American politics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_politics "American politics"), while [American values](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Americanism_(ideology) "Americanism (ideology)") are based on a democratic tradition inspired by the [American Enlightenment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Enlightenment "American Enlightenment") movement.

A [developed country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Developed_country "Developed country"), the [U.S. ranks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_rankings_of_the_United_States "International rankings of the United States") high in economic competitiveness, innovation, and [higher education](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Higher_education_in_the_United_States "Higher education in the United States"). Accounting for [over a quarter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal) "List of countries by GDP (nominal)") of nominal global GDP, [its economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy_of_the_United_States "Economy of the United States") has been the world's largest [since about 1890](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_largest_historical_GDP "List of countries by largest historical GDP"). It is the [wealthiest country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_total_wealth "List of countries by total wealth"), with the [highest disposable household income per capita](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disposable_household_and_per_capita_income#Household_disposable_income_per_capita_(OECD) "Disposable household and per capita income") among [OECD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OECD "OECD") members, though [its wealth inequality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wealth_inequality_in_the_United_States "Wealth inequality in the United States") is highly pronounced. Shaped by centuries of immigration, the [culture of the U.S.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_States "Culture of the United States") is diverse and [globally influential](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Americanization "Americanization"). Making up [more than a third](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_with_highest_military_expenditures "List of countries with highest military expenditures") of global military spending, the country has [one of the strongest militaries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces "United States Armed Forces") and is a designated [nuclear state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_state "Nuclear state"). A member of [numerous international organizations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_organization_membership_of_the_United_States "International organization membership of the United States"), the U.S. plays a major role in global political, cultural, economic, and military affairs.

Etymology
---------

Further information: [Names of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Names_of_the_United_States "Names of the United States"), [Demonyms for the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demonyms_for_the_United_States "Demonyms for the United States"), [United Colonies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Colonies "United Colonies"), and [Naming of the Americas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naming_of_the_Americas "Naming of the Americas")

Documented use of the phrase "United States of America" dates back to January 2, 1776. On that day, [Stephen Moylan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stephen_Moylan "Stephen Moylan"), a [Continental Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continental_Army "Continental Army") aide to General [George Washington](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Washington "George Washington"), wrote a letter to [Joseph Reed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Reed_(politician) "Joseph Reed (politician)"), Washington's [aide-de-camp](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aide-de-camp "Aide-de-camp"), seeking to go "with full and ample powers from the United States of America to Spain" to seek assistance in the [Revolutionary War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War "American Revolutionary War") effort.[[22]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-DeLear-20132-33)[[23]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-34) The first known public usage is an [anonymous essay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anonymous_work "Anonymous work") published in the [Williamsburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Williamsburg,_Virginia "Williamsburg, Virginia") newspaper _[The Virginia Gazette](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Virginia\_Gazette "The Virginia Gazette")_ on April 6, 1776.[[22]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-DeLear-20132-33) Sometime on or after June 11, 1776, [Thomas Jefferson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson "Thomas Jefferson") wrote "United States of America" in a rough draft of the [Declaration of Independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence "United States Declaration of Independence"),[[22]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-DeLear-20132-33) which was adopted by the [Second Continental Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Continental_Congress "Second Continental Congress") on July 4, 1776.[[24]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Davis72-35)

The term "United States" and its initialism "U.S.", used as nouns or as adjectives in English, are common short names for the country. The initialism "USA", a noun, is also common.[[25]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-36) "United States" and "U.S." are the established terms throughout the [U.S. federal government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States "Federal government of the United States"), with prescribed rules.[[l]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-38) "The States" is an established colloquial shortening of the name, used particularly from abroad;[[27]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-39) "stateside" is the corresponding adjective or adverb.[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-40)

"America" is the feminine form of the first word of _Americus Vesputius_, the Latinized name of Italian explorer [Amerigo Vespucci](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amerigo_Vespucci "Amerigo Vespucci") (1454â€“1512);[[m]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-41) it was first used as a place name by the German cartographers [Martin WaldseemÃ¼ller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martin_Waldseem%C3%BCller "Martin WaldseemÃ¼ller") and [Matthias Ringmann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matthias_Ringmann "Matthias Ringmann") in 1507.[[29]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-42)[[n]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-43) Vespucci first proposed that the [West Indies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Indies "West Indies") discovered by [Christopher Columbus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christopher_Columbus "Christopher Columbus") in 1492 were part of a previously unknown landmass and not among the Indies at the eastern limit of Asia.[[30]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-44)[[31]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-45)[[32]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-locnamingofamerica-46) In English, [the term "America"](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Americas_(terminology) "Americas (terminology)") usually does not refer to topics unrelated to the United States, despite the usage of "the [Americas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Americas "Americas")" to describe the totality of the continents of [North](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_America "North America") and [South America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_America "South America").[[33]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-47)

History
-------

Main article: [History of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States "History of the United States")

For a topical guide, see [Outline of the history of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Outline_of_the_history_of_the_United_States "Outline of the history of the United States").

### Indigenous peoples

Main articles: [History of Native Americans in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Native_Americans_in_the_United_States "History of Native Americans in the United States") and [Pre-Columbian era](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pre-Columbian_era "Pre-Columbian era")

[![Image 27](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Extreme_Makeover%2C_Mesa_Verde_Edition_-_panoramio.jpg/250px-Extreme_Makeover%2C_Mesa_Verde_Edition_-_panoramio.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Extreme_Makeover,_Mesa_Verde_Edition_-_panoramio.jpg)

[Cliff Palace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cliff_Palace "Cliff Palace"), a settlement of [ancestors of](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancestral_Puebloans "Ancestral Puebloans") the [Native American](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States "Native Americans in the United States")[Pueblo peoples](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pueblo_peoples "Pueblo peoples") in present-day [Montezuma County, Colorado](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Montezuma_County,_Colorado "Montezuma County, Colorado"), built between c. 1200 and 1275[[34]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-48)

The [first inhabitants of North America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paleo-Indians "Paleo-Indians") migrated from [Siberia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siberia "Siberia") over 12,000 years ago, either across the [Bering land bridge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bering_land_bridge "Bering land bridge") or along the [now-submerged Ice Age coastline](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coastal_migration_(Americas) "Coastal migration (Americas)").[[35]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEErlandsonRickVellanoweth200819-49)[[36]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTESavage201155%E2%80%9358-50) The [Clovis culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clovis_culture "Clovis culture"), which appeared around 11,000 BC, is believed to be the first widespread culture in the Americas.[[37]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWatersStafford20071122%E2%80%931126-51)[[38]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlannery2015173%E2%80%93185-52) Over time, Indigenous North American cultures grew increasingly sophisticated, and some, such as the [Mississippian culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mississippian_culture "Mississippian culture"), developed [agriculture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Agricultural_Complex "Eastern Agricultural Complex"), [architecture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southeastern_Ceremonial_Complex "Southeastern Ceremonial Complex"), and [complex societies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Complex_societies "Complex societies").[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTELockard2010315-53) In the [post-archaic period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Native_Americans_in_the_United_States#Post-Archaic_stage "History of Native Americans in the United States"), the Mississippian cultures were located in the [midwestern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Midwestern_United_States "Midwestern United States"), [eastern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_United_States "Eastern United States"), and [southern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_United_States "Southern United States") regions, and the [Algonquian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algonquian_peoples "Algonquian peoples") in the [Great Lakes region](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Lakes_region "Great Lakes region") and along the [Eastern Seaboard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States "East Coast of the United States"), while the [Hohokam culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hohokam_culture "Hohokam culture") and [Ancestral Puebloans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancestral_Puebloans "Ancestral Puebloans") inhabited the [Southwest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Southwest "American Southwest").[[40]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-54)[Native population estimates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population_history_of_the_Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas "Population history of the Indigenous peoples of the Americas") of what is now the United States before the arrival of European immigrants range from around 500,000[[41]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThornton199834-55)[[42]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerdueGreen200540-56) to nearly 10 million.[[42]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerdueGreen200540-56)[[43]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHainesHainesSteckel200012-57)

### European exploration, colonization and conflict (1513â€“1765)

Main articles: [Colonial history of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonial_history_of_the_United_States "Colonial history of the United States") and [Colonial American military history](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonial_American_military_history "Colonial American military history")

[![Image 28](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Nouvelle-France_map-en.svg/330px-Nouvelle-France_map-en.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Nouvelle-France_map-en.svg)

The [colonial possessions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonial_history_of_the_United_States "Colonial history of the United States") of [Britain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_colonization_of_the_Americas "British colonization of the Americas") (the Thirteen Colonies in pink and others in purple), [France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_France "New France") (in blue), and [Spain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Spain "Kingdom of Spain") (in orange) in North America, 1750

[Christopher Columbus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christopher_Columbus "Christopher Columbus") began exploring the [Caribbean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caribbean "Caribbean") for Spain in 1492, leading to [Spanish-speaking settlements and missions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Empire "Spanish Empire") from what are now [Puerto Rico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puerto_Rico "Puerto Rico") and [Florida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Florida "Spanish Florida") to [New Mexico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santa_Fe_de_Nuevo_M%C3%A9xico "Santa Fe de Nuevo MÃ©xico") and [California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alta_California "Alta California"). The first Spanish colony in the present-day continental United States was [Spanish Florida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Florida "Spanish Florida"), chartered in 1513.[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Galloway2006-58)[[45]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Hudson2018-59)[[46]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-60)[[47]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-61) After several settlements failed there due to starvation and disease, Spain's first permanent town, [Saint Augustine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saint_Augustine,_Florida "Saint Augustine, Florida"), was founded in 1565.[[48]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-62)

France established its own settlements in [French Florida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Florida "French Florida") in 1562, but they were either abandoned (Charlesfort, 1578) or destroyed by Spanish raids ([Fort Caroline](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fort_Caroline "Fort Caroline"), 1565). [Permanent French settlements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_France "New France") were founded much later along the [Great Lakes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Lakes "Great Lakes") ([Fort Detroit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fort_Pontchartrain_du_D%C3%A9troit "Fort Pontchartrain du DÃ©troit"), 1701), the [Mississippi River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mississippi_River "Mississippi River") (Saint Louis, 1764) and especially the [Gulf of Mexico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico "Gulf of Mexico") ([New Orleans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Orleans "New Orleans"), 1718).[[49]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Petto20072-63) Early European colonies also included the thriving Dutch colony of [New Nederland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Nederland "New Nederland") (settled 1626, present-day New York) and the small Swedish colony of [New Sweden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Sweden "New Sweden") (settled 1638 in what became Delaware). [British colonization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_colonization_of_the_Americas "British colonization of the Americas") of the [East Coast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States "East Coast of the United States") began with the [Virginia Colony](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colony_of_Virginia "Colony of Virginia") (1607) and the [Plymouth Colony](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plymouth_Colony "Plymouth Colony") (Massachusetts, 1620).[[50]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Jr.Selby20182-64)[[51]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-BellahSullivan20062-65)

The [Mayflower Compact](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mayflower_Compact "Mayflower Compact") in Massachusetts and the [Fundamental Orders of Connecticut](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fundamental_Orders_of_Connecticut "Fundamental Orders of Connecticut") established precedents for local representative [self-governance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-governance "Self-governance") and [constitutionalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitutionalism "Constitutionalism") that would develop throughout the American colonies.[[52]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Remini2%E2%80%9332-66)[[53]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Johnson26%E2%80%93302-67) While European settlers in what is now the United States experienced conflicts with Native Americans, they also engaged in trade, exchanging European tools for food and animal pelts.[[54]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-68)[[o]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-72) Relations ranged from close cooperation to warfare and massacres. The colonial authorities often pursued policies that forced Native Americans to adopt European lifestyles, including conversion to Christianity.[[58]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-73)[[59]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-74) Along the eastern seaboard, settlers [trafficked African slaves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slavery_in_the_colonial_history_of_the_United_States "Slavery in the colonial history of the United States") through the [Atlantic slave trade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade "Atlantic slave trade").[[60]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-75)

The original [Thirteen Colonies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies "Thirteen Colonies")[[p]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-76) that would later found the United States were administered as possessions of the [British Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Empire "British Empire") by Crown-appointed governors,[[61]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-BilhartzElliott20072-77) though [local governments held elections open to most white male property owners](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonial_government_in_the_Thirteen_Colonies "Colonial government in the Thirteen Colonies").[[62]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Wood19982-78)[[63]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-79) The colonial population grew rapidly from Maine to Georgia, eclipsing Native American populations;[[64]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-80) by the 1770s, the natural increase of the population was such that only a small minority of Americans had been born overseas.[[65]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-81) The colonies' distance from Britain facilitated the entrenchment of self-governance,[[66]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-82) and the [First Great Awakening](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Great_Awakening "First Great Awakening"), a series of [Christian revivals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_revival "Christian revival"), fueled colonial interest in guaranteed [religious liberty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_religion "Freedom of religion").[[67]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-83)

### American Revolution and the early republic (1765â€“1800)

Main articles: [History of the United States (1776â€“1789)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_(1776%E2%80%931789) "History of the United States (1776â€“1789)"), [History of the United States (1789â€“1815)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_(1789%E2%80%931815) "History of the United States (1789â€“1815)"), [American Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Revolution "American Revolution"), and [Founding Fathers of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Founding_Fathers_of_the_United_States "Founding Fathers of the United States")

[![Image 29: See caption](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Declaration_of_Independence_%281819%29%2C_by_John_Trumbull.jpg/250px-Declaration_of_Independence_%281819%29%2C_by_John_Trumbull.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Declaration_of_Independence_(1819),_by_John_Trumbull.jpg)

The _[Declaration of Independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Declaration\_of\_Independence\_(painting) "Declaration of Independence (painting)")_ portrait depicts the [Committee of Five](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Committee_of_Five "Committee of Five") presenting [the Declaration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence "United States Declaration of Independence") to the [Continental Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Continental_Congress "Second Continental Congress") on June 28, 1776, in [Philadelphia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philadelphia "Philadelphia").

Following their victory in the [French and Indian War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_and_Indian_War "French and Indian War"), Britain began to assert greater control over local colonial affairs, resulting in [colonial political resistance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Revolution "American Revolution"); one of the primary colonial grievances was a denial of their [rights as Englishmen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rights_of_Englishmen "Rights of Englishmen"), particularly the right to [representation in the British government that taxed them](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/No_taxation_without_representation "No taxation without representation"). To demonstrate their dissatisfaction and resolve, the [First Continental Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Continental_Congress "First Continental Congress") met in 1774 and passed the [Continental Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continental_Association "Continental Association"), a colonial boycott of British goods enforced by local "[committees of safety](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Committee_of_safety_(American_Revolution) "Committee of safety (American Revolution)")" that proved effective. The British attempt to then disarm the colonists resulted in the 1775 [Battles of Lexington and Concord](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battles_of_Lexington_and_Concord "Battles of Lexington and Concord"), igniting the [American Revolutionary War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War "American Revolutionary War"). At the [Second Continental Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Continental_Congress "Second Continental Congress"), the colonies appointed [George Washington](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Washington "George Washington") commander-in-chief of the [Continental Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continental_Army "Continental Army"), and created [a committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Committee_of_Five "Committee of Five") that named [Thomas Jefferson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson "Thomas Jefferson") to draft the [Declaration of Independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence "United States Declaration of Independence"). Two days after passing the [Lee Resolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lee_Resolution "Lee Resolution") to create an independent nation the Declaration was adopted on July 4, 1776.[[68]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-YoungNash20112-84) The [political values of the American Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Enlightenment "American Enlightenment") evolved beyond an armed rebellion demanding reform within an empire to a revolution that created an entirely new social and governing system founded on the defense of [liberty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberty "Liberty") and the protection of [inalienable individual rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_rights_and_legal_rights "Natural rights and legal rights"); [sovereignty of the people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Popular_sovereignty "Popular sovereignty");[[69]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-85)[republicanism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republicanism_in_the_United_States "Republicanism in the United States") over [monarchy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monarchy "Monarchy"), [aristocracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aristocracy "Aristocracy"), and other hereditary political power; [civic virtue](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civic_virtue "Civic virtue"); and an intolerance of [political corruption](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_corruption "Political corruption").[[70]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-86) The [Founding Fathers of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Founding_Fathers_of_the_United_States "Founding Fathers of the United States"), who included Washington, Jefferson, [John Adams](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Adams "John Adams"), [Benjamin Franklin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benjamin_Franklin "Benjamin Franklin"), [Alexander Hamilton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_Hamilton "Alexander Hamilton"), [John Jay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Jay "John Jay"), [James Madison](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Madison "James Madison"), [Thomas Paine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Paine "Thomas Paine"), and many others, were inspired by [Classical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Classical_republicanism#Classical_antecedents "Classical republicanism"), [Renaissance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Renaissance_philosophy "Renaissance philosophy"), and [Enlightenment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment#Politics "Age of Enlightenment") philosophies and ideas.[[71]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-87)[[72]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-SEoP-2006-88)

Though in practical effect since its drafting in 1777, the [Articles of Confederation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Articles_of_Confederation "Articles of Confederation") was ratified in 1781 and formally established a decentralized government that operated until 1789.[[68]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-YoungNash20112-84) After the British surrender at the [siege of Yorktown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Yorktown "Siege of Yorktown") in 1781, American sovereignty was internationally recognized by the [Treaty of Paris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783) "Treaty of Paris (1783)") (1783), through which the U.S. gained territory stretching west to the Mississippi River, north to present-day Canada, and south to [Spanish Florida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Florida "Spanish Florida").[[73]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-89) The [Northwest Ordinance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northwest_Ordinance "Northwest Ordinance") (1787) established the precedent by which the country's territory would expand with the [admission of new states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Admission_to_the_Union "Admission to the Union"), rather than the expansion of existing states.[[74]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-90)

The [U.S. Constitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_the_United_States "Constitution of the United States") was drafted at the 1787 [Constitutional Convention](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitutional_Convention_(United_States) "Constitutional Convention (United States)") to overcome the limitations of the Articles. It went into effect in 1789, creating a [federal republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_republic "Federal republic") governed by [three separate branches](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Separation_of_powers_under_the_United_States_Constitution "Separation of powers under the United States Constitution") that together formed a system of [checks and balances](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Checks_and_balances "Checks and balances").[[75]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFoner2020524-91) George Washington [was elected](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1788%E2%80%9389_United_States_presidential_election "1788â€“89 United States presidential election") the country's first president under the Constitution, and the [Bill of Rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Bill_of_Rights "United States Bill of Rights") was adopted in 1791 to allay skeptics' concerns about the power of the more centralized government.[[76]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFoner2020538%E2%80%93540-92)[His resignation as commander-in-chief](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Washington%27s_resignation_as_commander-in-chief "George Washington's resignation as commander-in-chief") after the Revolutionary War and his later refusal to run for a third term as the country's first president established a precedent for the supremacy of civil authority in the United States and the [peaceful transfer of power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peaceful_transition_of_power "Peaceful transition of power").[[77]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-BoyerJr.20072-93)

### Westward expansion and Civil War (1800â€“1865)

Main articles: [History of the United States (1815â€“1849)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_(1815%E2%80%931849) "History of the United States (1815â€“1849)") and [History of the United States (1849â€“1865)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_(1849%E2%80%931865) "History of the United States (1849â€“1865)")

[![Image 30: Historical territorial expansion of the United States](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/U.S._Territorial_Acquisitions.png/330px-U.S._Territorial_Acquisitions.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:U.S._Territorial_Acquisitions.png)

[Territorial expansion of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Territorial_evolution_of_the_United_States "Territorial evolution of the United States")

In the late 18th century, American settlers began to [expand westward](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Territorial_evolution_of_the_United_States "Territorial evolution of the United States") in larger numbers, many with a sense of [manifest destiny](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manifest_destiny "Manifest destiny").[[78]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-MD20072-94)[[79]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson198841%E2%80%9346-95) The [Louisiana Purchase](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase "Louisiana Purchase") of 1803 from France nearly doubled the territory of the United States.[[80]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-96)[[81]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-97)[Lingering issues with Britain remained](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Origins_of_the_War_of_1812 "Origins of the War of 1812"), leading to the [War of 1812](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_of_1812 "War of 1812"), which was fought to a draw.[[82]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Wait19992-98)[Spain ceded Florida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adams%E2%80%93On%C3%ADs_Treaty "Adamsâ€“OnÃ­s Treaty") and its Gulf Coast territory in 1819.[[83]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-KloseJones19942-99)

The [Missouri Compromise](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Missouri_Compromise "Missouri Compromise") of 1820, which admitted [Missouri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Missouri "Missouri") as a [slave state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slave_states_and_free_states "Slave states and free states") and [Maine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maine#Statehood "Maine") as a free state, attempted to balance the desire of northern states to prevent the expansion of slavery into new territories with that of southern states to extend it there. Primarily, the compromise prohibited slavery in all other lands of the Louisiana Purchase north of the [36Â°30â€² parallel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parallel_36%C2%B030%E2%80%B2_north "Parallel 36Â°30â€² north").[[84]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-100)

As Americans expanded further into territory inhabited by Native Americans, the [federal government implemented policies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Indian_Policy "Federal Indian Policy") of [Indian removal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_removal "Indian removal") or [assimilation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultural_assimilation_of_Native_Americans "Cultural assimilation of Native Americans").[[85]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-101)[[86]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-102) The most significant such legislation was the [Indian Removal Act of 1830](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Removal_Act "Indian Removal Act"), a key policy of President [Andrew Jackson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrew_Jackson "Andrew Jackson"). It resulted in the [Trail of Tears](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trail_of_Tears "Trail of Tears") (1830â€“1850), in which an estimated 60,000 Native Americans living east of the [Mississippi River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mississippi_River "Mississippi River") were forcibly removed and displaced to lands far to the west, causing 13,200 to 16,700 deaths along the forced march.[[87]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson198845-103) Settler expansion as well as this influx of Indigenous peoples from the East resulted in the [American Indian Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Indian_Wars "American Indian Wars") west of the Mississippi.[[88]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-104)[[89]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-BillingtonRidge2001j2-105)

During the colonial period, [slavery became legal in all the Thirteen colonies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slavery_in_the_colonial_history_of_the_United_States "Slavery in the colonial history of the United States"), but by 1770 it provided the main labor force in the [large-scale](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plantation_complexes_in_the_Southern_United_States "Plantation complexes in the Southern United States"), [agriculture-dependent economies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antebellum_South#Economic_structure "Antebellum South") of the [Southern Colonies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Colonies "Southern Colonies") from Maryland to Georgia. The practice began to be significantly questioned during the American Revolution, [[90]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWalker_Howe200752%E2%80%9354Wright2022-106) and spurred by an active [abolitionist movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_States "Abolitionism in the United States") that had reemerged in the 1830s, states in [the North](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_United_States "Northern United States") enacted laws to prohibit slavery within their boundaries.[[91]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWalker_Howe200752%E2%80%9354Rodriguez2015XXXIVWright2022-107) At the same time, [support for slavery had strengthened in Southern states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pro-slavery_ideology_in_the_United_States "Pro-slavery ideology in the United States"), with widespread use of inventions such as the [cotton gin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cotton_gin "Cotton gin") (1793) having made slavery immensely profitable for [Southern elites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planter_class "Planter class").[[92]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-108)[[93]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-109)[[94]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWalker_Howe2007478,_481%E2%80%93482,_587%E2%80%93588-110)

The United States [annexed the Republic of Texas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texas_annexation "Texas annexation") in 1845,[[95]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Morrison19992-111) and the 1846 [Oregon Treaty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oregon_Treaty "Oregon Treaty") led to U.S. control of the present-day [American Northwest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northwestern_United_States "Northwestern United States").[[96]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Kemp20102-112) Dispute with Mexico over Texas led to the [Mexicanâ€“American War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War "Mexicanâ€“American War") (1846â€“1848). After the victory of the U.S., Mexico recognized U.S. sovereignty over Texas, [New Mexico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Mexico "New Mexico"), and [California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California "California") in the 1848 [Mexican Cession](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexican_Cession "Mexican Cession"); the cession's lands also included the future states of [Nevada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nevada "Nevada"), [Colorado](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colorado "Colorado") and [Utah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Utah "Utah").[[78]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-MD20072-94)[[97]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-McIlwraithMuller20012-113) The [California gold rush](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_gold_rush "California gold rush") of 1848â€“1849 spurred a huge migration of white settlers to the Pacific coast, leading to even more confrontations with Native populations. One of the most violent, the [California genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_genocide "California genocide") of thousands of Native inhabitants, lasted into the mid-1870s.[[98]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-114) Additional western territories and states were created.[[99]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Rawls1999-115)

[![Image 31](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/US_SlaveFree1858.gif/330px-US_SlaveFree1858.gif)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:US_SlaveFree1858.gif)

[Slave states and free states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slave_states_and_free_states "Slave states and free states") in 1858

Throughout the 1850s, the [sectional conflict regarding slavery](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slave_states_and_free_states "Slave states and free states") was further inflamed by national legislation in the U.S. Congress and decisions of the Supreme Court. In Congress, the [Fugitive Slave Act of 1850](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fugitive_Slave_Act_of_1850 "Fugitive Slave Act of 1850") mandated the forcible return to their owners in the South of slaves taking refuge in non-slave states, while the [Kansasâ€“Nebraska Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kansas%E2%80%93Nebraska_Act "Kansasâ€“Nebraska Act") of 1854 effectively gutted the anti-slavery requirements of the Missouri Compromise.[[100]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-116) In its [Dred Scott decision](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dred_Scott_v._Sandford "Dred Scott v. Sandford") of 1857, the Supreme Court ruled against a slave brought into non-slave territory, simultaneously declaring the entire Missouri Compromise to be unconstitutional. These and other [events exacerbated tensions between North and South](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Origins_of_the_American_Civil_War "Origins of the American Civil War") that would culminate in the [American Civil War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Civil_War "American Civil War") (1861â€“1865).[[101]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-117)[[102]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Woods_2012_pp._415%E2%80%934392-118)

Beginning with [South Carolina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Carolina "South Carolina"), 11 slave-state governments voted to [secede from the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secession_in_the_United_States "Secession in the United States") in 1861, joining to create the [Confederate States of America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America "Confederate States of America"). All other state governments remained loyal to [the Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War) "Union (American Civil War)").[[q]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-119)[[103]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Silkenat_2019_p._252-120)[[104]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988236-121) War broke out in April 1861 after the Confederacy [bombarded Fort Sumter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Sumter "Battle of Fort Sumter").[[105]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-122)[[106]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988273%E2%80%93274-123) Following the [Emancipation Proclamation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emancipation_Proclamation "Emancipation Proclamation") on January 1, 1863, many freed slaves joined the [Union army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Union_army "Union army").[[107]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-124) The war [began to turn in the Union's favor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turning_point_of_the_American_Civil_War "Turning point of the American Civil War") following the 1863 [Siege of Vicksburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Vicksburg "Siege of Vicksburg") and [Battle of Gettysburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Gettysburg "Battle of Gettysburg"), and the Confederates surrendered in 1865 after the Union's victory in the [Battle of Appomattox Court House](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Appomattox_Court_House "Battle of Appomattox Court House").[[108]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-125)

### Reconstruction, Gilded Age, and Progressive Era (1866â€“1917)

Main article: [History of the United States (1865â€“1917)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_(1865%E2%80%931917) "History of the United States (1865â€“1917)")

[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Emigrants_(i.e._immigrants)_landing_at_Ellis_Island_-.webm "Play video")Duration: 2 minutes and 27 seconds.2:27[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Emigrants_(i.e._immigrants)_landing_at_Ellis_Island_-.webm)

An [Edison Studios](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edison_Studios "Edison Studios") film showing immigrants arriving at [Ellis Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ellis_Island "Ellis Island") in [New York Harbor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Harbor "New York Harbor"), a major point of entry for European [immigrants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immigration_to_the_United_States "Immigration to the United States") in the late 19th and early 20th centuries[[109]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-PriceBenton-Short2008-126)[[110]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-127)

Efforts toward [reconstruction in the secessionist South](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reconstruction_era "Reconstruction era") had begun as early as 1862,[[111]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDubois1935163-128) but it was only after [President Lincoln's assassination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assassination_of_Abraham_Lincoln "Assassination of Abraham Lincoln") that the three [Reconstruction Amendments](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reconstruction_Amendments "Reconstruction Amendments") to the Constitution were ratified [to protect civil rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_rights_movement_(1865%E2%80%931896) "Civil rights movement (1865â€“1896)"). The amendments codified nationally the abolition of slavery and involuntary servitude except as punishment for crimes, promised equal protection under the law for all persons, and prohibited discrimination on the basis of race or previous enslavement.[[112]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-129)[[113]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFoner198866-7,_251-261,_446-449-130)[[114]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-131) As a result, African Americans took an active political role in ex-Confederate states in the decade following the Civil War.[[115]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFoner1988xxv-132)[[116]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDubois1935381-727-133) The former Confederate states were readmitted to the Union, beginning with Tennessee in 1866 and ending with Georgia in 1870.[[117]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-134)[[118]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-135)

National infrastructure, including [transcontinental telegraph](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_transcontinental_telegraph "First transcontinental telegraph") and [railroads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_transcontinental_railroad "First transcontinental railroad"), spurred growth in the [American frontier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_frontier "American frontier"). This was accelerated by the [Homestead Acts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homestead_Acts "Homestead Acts"), through which nearly 10 percent of the total land area of the United States was given away free to some 1.6 million homesteaders.[[119]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Black2011kj2-136)[[120]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-137) From 1865 through 1917, an unprecedented stream of [immigrants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immigrants "Immigrants") arrived in the United States, including 24.4 million from Europe.[[121]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-138) Most came through the [Port of New York](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Port_of_New_York_and_New_Jersey "Port of New York and New Jersey"), and New York City and other large cities on the [East Coast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States "East Coast of the United States") became home to large [Jewish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_the_United_States "History of the Jews in the United States"), [Irish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irish_Americans "Irish Americans"), and [Italian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_Americans "Italian Americans") populations. Many [Northern Europeans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Europe "Northern Europe") as well as significant numbers of [Germans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_Americans "German Americans") and other [Central Europeans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Europe "Central Europe") moved to the [Midwest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Midwestern_United_States "Midwestern United States"). At the same time, about one million [French Canadians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French-Canadian_Americans "French-Canadian Americans") migrated from [Quebec](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quebec "Quebec") to [New England](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_England "New England").[[122]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-139) During the [Great Migration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Migration_(African_American) "Great Migration (African American)"), millions of African Americans [left the rural South](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jim_Crow_economy "Jim Crow economy") for urban areas in the North.[[123]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-140)[Alaska was purchased](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alaska_Purchase "Alaska Purchase") from [Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Empire "Russian Empire") in 1867.[[124]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-141)

The [Compromise of 1877](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compromise_of_1877 "Compromise of 1877") is generally considered the end of the Reconstruction era, as it resolved the electoral crisis following the [1876 presidential election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1876_United_States_presidential_election "1876 United States presidential election") and led President [Rutherford B. Hayes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rutherford_B._Hayes "Rutherford B. Hayes") to reduce the role of federal troops in the South.[[125]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFoner1988xxvii,_575-587-142) Immediately, the [Redeemers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Redeemers "Redeemers") began evicting the [Carpetbaggers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carpetbaggers "Carpetbaggers") and quickly regained local control of Southern politics in the name of [white supremacy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_supremacy "White supremacy").[[126]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-143)[[127]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-144) African Americans endured a period of heightened, overt racism following Reconstruction, a time often considered the [nadir of American race relations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nadir_of_American_race_relations "Nadir of American race relations").[[128]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-ReferenceA2-145)[[129]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-146) A series of Supreme Court decisions, including _[Plessy v. Ferguson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plessy\_v.\_Ferguson "Plessy v. Ferguson")_, emptied the [Fourteenth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fourteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution "Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution") and [Fifteenth Amendments](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fifteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution "Fifteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution") of their force, allowing [Jim Crow laws](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jim_Crow_laws "Jim Crow laws") in the South to remain unchecked, [sundown towns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sundown_town "Sundown town") in the Midwest, and [segregation in communities across the country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Racial_segregation_in_the_United_States "Racial segregation in the United States"), which would be reinforced in part by the policy of [redlining](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Redlining "Redlining") later adopted by the federal [Home Owners' Loan Corporation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Home_Owners%27_Loan_Corporation "Home Owners' Loan Corporation").[[130]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-147)

[An explosion of technological advancement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Industrial_Revolution "Second Industrial Revolution") accompanied by the exploitation of cheap immigrant labor[[131]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-148) led to [rapid economic expansion during the late 19th and early 20th centuries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gilded_Age "Gilded Age"), allowing the United States to outpace the economies of England, France, and Germany combined.[[132]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-149)[[133]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-150) This fostered the amassing of power by [a few prominent industrialists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robber_baron_(industrialist) "Robber baron (industrialist)"), largely by their formation of [trusts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trust_(business) "Trust (business)") and [monopolies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monopoly "Monopoly") to prevent competition.[[134]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Atlantic2-151)[Tycoons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tycoon "Tycoon") led the nation's expansion in the [railroad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_rail_transportation_in_the_United_States "History of rail transportation in the United States"), [petroleum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_petroleum_industry_in_the_United_States "History of the petroleum industry in the United States"), and [steel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_steel_industry_(1850%E2%80%931970) "History of the steel industry (1850â€“1970)") industries. The United States emerged as a pioneer of the [automotive industry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States "Automotive industry in the United States").[[135]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-152) These changes resulted in significant increases in [economic inequality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_inequality "Economic inequality"), [slum conditions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/How_the_Other_Half_Lives "How the Other Half Lives"), and [social unrest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_incidents_of_civil_unrest_in_the_United_States "List of incidents of civil unrest in the United States"), creating the environment for [labor unions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labor_history_of_the_United_States "Labor history of the United States") and [socialist movements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_socialist_movement_in_the_United_States "History of the socialist movement in the United States") to begin to flourish.[[136]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-153)[[137]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-154)[[138]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Fraser2-155) This period eventually ended with the advent of the [Progressive Era](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Progressive_Era "Progressive Era"), which was characterized by significant reforms.[[139]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Aldrich2-156)[[140]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-157)

Pro-American elements in Hawaii [overthrew the Hawaiian monarchy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Overthrow_of_the_Hawaiian_Kingdom "Overthrow of the Hawaiian Kingdom"); the islands [were annexed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newlands_Resolution "Newlands Resolution") in 1898. That same year, [Puerto Rico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puerto_Rico "Puerto Rico"), [the Philippines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Philippines "The Philippines"), and [Guam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guam "Guam") were ceded to the U.S. by Spain after the latter's defeat in the [Spanishâ€“American War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War "Spanishâ€“American War"). (The Philippines was granted full independence from the U.S. on July 4, 1946, following World War II. Puerto Rico and Guam have remained U.S. territories.)[[141]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-158)[American Samoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Samoa "American Samoa") was acquired by the United States in 1900 after the [Second Samoan Civil War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Samoan_Civil_War "Second Samoan Civil War").[[142]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-159) The [U.S. Virgin Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands "United States Virgin Islands") were purchased from [Denmark](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denmark "Denmark") in 1917.[[143]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-160)

### World War I, Great Depression, and World War II (1917â€“1945)

Main article: [History of the United States (1917â€“1945)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_(1917%E2%80%931945) "History of the United States (1917â€“1945)")

[![Image 32](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Trinity_shot_color_%284x3_cropped%29.jpg/250px-Trinity_shot_color_%284x3_cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Trinity_shot_color_(4x3_cropped).jpg)

The 1945 American [Trinity test](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trinity_(nuclear_test) "Trinity (nuclear test)"), the first-ever detonation of a [nuclear weapon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_weapon "Nuclear weapon")

The United States [entered World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_entry_into_World_War_I "American entry into World War I") alongside the [Allies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I "Allies of World War I") in 1917 helping to turn the tide against the [Central Powers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Powers "Central Powers").[[144]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-161) In 1920, [a constitutional amendment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nineteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution "Nineteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution") granted nationwide [women's suffrage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women%27s_suffrage_in_the_United_States "Women's suffrage in the United States").[[145]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-162) During the 1920s and 1930s, radio for [mass communication](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass_communication "Mass communication") and early television transformed communications nationwide.[[146]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinchester2013410%E2%80%93411-163) The [Wall Street Crash of 1929](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wall_Street_Crash_of_1929 "Wall Street Crash of 1929") triggered the [Great Depression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Depression_in_the_United_States "Great Depression in the United States"), to which President [Franklin D. Roosevelt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt "Franklin D. Roosevelt") responded with the [New Deal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Deal "New Deal") plan of "reform, recovery and relief", a series of unprecedented and sweeping [recovery programs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alphabet_agencies "Alphabet agencies") and [employment relief projects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Works_Progress_Administration "Works Progress Administration") combined with [financial reforms and regulations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regulatory_economics "Regulatory economics").[[147]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-164)[[148]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-165)

[Initially neutral](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_non-interventionism_before_entering_World_War_II "United States non-interventionism before entering World War II") during [World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_history_of_the_United_States_during_World_War_II "Military history of the United States during World War II"), the U.S. began [supplying war materiel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lend-Lease "Lend-Lease") to the [Allies of World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II "Allies of World War II") in March 1941 and [entered the war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_entry_into_World_War_II "American entry into World War II") in December after [Japan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empire_of_Japan "Empire of Japan")'s [attack on Pearl Harbor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor "Attack on Pearl Harbor").[[149]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Pearl_Harbor2-166) Agreeing to a "[Europe first](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Europe_first "Europe first")" policy, the U.S. concentrated its wartime efforts on Japan's allies [Italy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fascist_Italy "Fascist Italy") and [Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany") until their final defeat in May 1945. The U.S. [developed the first nuclear weapons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manhattan_Project "Manhattan Project") and [used them against the Japanese cities of Hiroshima and Nagasaki](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki "Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki") in August 1945, ending the war.[[150]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-167)[[151]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-168) The United States was one of the "[Four Policemen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Four_Policemen "Four Policemen")" who met to plan the [post-war world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aftermath_of_World_War_II "Aftermath of World War II"), alongside the [United Kingdom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom "United Kingdom"), the [Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union"), and [China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%931949) "Republic of China (1912â€“1949)").[[152]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoopesBrinkley1997100-169)[[153]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis197225-170) The U.S. emerged relatively unscathed from the war, with even greater [economic power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_power "Economic power") and [international political influence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sphere_of_influence "Sphere of influence").[[154]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-171)

### Cold War and social revolution (1945â€“1991)

Main articles: [History of the United States (1945â€“1964)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_(1945%E2%80%931964) "History of the United States (1945â€“1964)"), [History of the United States (1964â€“1980)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_(1964%E2%80%931980) "History of the United States (1964â€“1980)"), and [History of the United States (1980â€“1991)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_(1980%E2%80%931991) "History of the United States (1980â€“1991)")

[![Image 33](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Civil_Rights_March_on_Washington%2C_D.C._%28Leaders_marching_from_the_Washington_Monument_to_the_Lincoln_Memorial%29_-_NARA_-_542010.jpg/250px-Civil_Rights_March_on_Washington%2C_D.C._%28Leaders_marching_from_the_Washington_Monument_to_the_Lincoln_Memorial%29_-_NARA_-_542010.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Civil_Rights_March_on_Washington,_D.C._(Leaders_marching_from_the_Washington_Monument_to_the_Lincoln_Memorial)_-_NARA_-_542010.jpg)

Civil rights activists during the [March on Washington for Jobs and Freedom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/March_on_Washington_for_Jobs_and_Freedom "March on Washington for Jobs and Freedom") in [Washington, D.C.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington,_D.C. "Washington, D.C.") in August 1963

The end of [World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II "World War II") in 1945 left the U.S. and the [Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union") as [superpowers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superpower "Superpower"), each with its own political, military, and economic [sphere of influence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sphere_of_influence "Sphere of influence"). Geopolitical tensions between the two superpowers soon led to the [Cold War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War "Cold War").[[155]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Blakemore-20192-172)[[156]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-173)[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-174) The U.S. implemented a policy of [containment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Containment "Containment") intended to limit the Soviet Union's sphere of influence; engaged in [regime change against governments perceived to be aligned with the Soviets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_involvement_in_regime_change#1945%E2%80%931991:_Cold_War "United States involvement in regime change"); and prevailed in the [Space Race](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_Race "Space Race"), which culminated with the [first crewed Moon landing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_11 "Apollo 11") in 1969.[[158]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-175)[[159]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Proxy2-176)

Domestically, the U.S. [experienced economic growth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Post%E2%80%93World_War_II_economic_expansion "Postâ€“World War II economic expansion"), [urbanization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urbanization_in_the_United_States "Urbanization in the United States"), and [population growth following World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mid-20th_century_baby_boom "Mid-20th century baby boom").[[160]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinchester2013305%E2%80%93308-177) The [civil rights movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_rights_movement "Civil rights movement") emerged, with [Martin Luther King Jr.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martin_Luther_King_Jr. "Martin Luther King Jr.") becoming a prominent leader in the early 1960s.[[161]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-178) The [Great Society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Society "Great Society") plan of President [Lyndon B. Johnson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson "Lyndon B. Johnson")'s administration resulted in groundbreaking and broad-reaching laws, policies and [a constitutional amendment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twenty-fourth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution "Twenty-fourth Amendment to the United States Constitution") to counteract some of the worst effects of lingering [institutional racism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institutional_racism "Institutional racism").[[162]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-179)
