The [counterculture movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Counterculture_of_the_1960s "Counterculture of the 1960s") in the U.S. brought significant social changes, including the liberalization of attitudes toward [recreational drug use](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recreational_drug_use "Recreational drug use") and [sexuality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_revolution "Sexual revolution").[[163]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-180)[[164]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-181) It also encouraged [open defiance of the military draft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Draft_evasion_in_the_Vietnam_War "Draft evasion in the Vietnam War") (leading to the [end of conscription](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conscription_in_the_United_States "Conscription in the United States") in 1973)[[165]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-182) and [wide opposition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opposition_to_United_States_involvement_in_the_Vietnam_War "Opposition to United States involvement in the Vietnam War") to [U.S. intervention in Vietnam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_in_the_Vietnam_War "United States in the Vietnam War"), with the U.S. totally withdrawing in 1975.[[166]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-183)[A societal shift in the roles of women](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women%27s_liberation_movement_in_the_United_States "Women's liberation movement in the United States") was significantly responsible for the large increase in female paid labor participation starting in the 1970s, and by 1985 the majority of American women aged 16 and older were employed.[[167]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-184)

The [Fall of Communism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989 "Revolutions of 1989") and the [dissolution of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union "Dissolution of the Soviet Union") from 1989 to 1991 marked the [end of the Cold War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/End_of_the_Cold_War "End of the Cold War") and [left the United States as the world's sole superpower](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superpower#After_the_Cold_War "Superpower").[[168]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Gaidar2-185)[[169]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-186)[[170]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-187)[[171]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-188) This cemented the United States' global influence, reinforcing the concept of the "[American Century](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Century "American Century")" as the U.S. dominated international political, cultural, economic, and military affairs.[[172]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-189)[[173]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-190)

### Contemporary (1991â€“present)

Main articles: [History of the United States (1991â€“2016)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_(1991%E2%80%932016) "History of the United States (1991â€“2016)") and [History of the United States (2016â€“present)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_(2016%E2%80%93present) "History of the United States (2016â€“present)")

[![Image 34](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/WTC_smoking_on_9-11.jpeg/250px-WTC_smoking_on_9-11.jpeg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:WTC_smoking_on_9-11.jpeg)

The [Twin Towers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Trade_Center_(1973%E2%80%932001) "World Trade Center (1973â€“2001)") in New York City during the [September 11 attacks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/September_11_attacks "September 11 attacks") of 2001

The 1990s saw the [longest recorded economic expansion in American history](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1990s_United_States_boom "1990s United States boom"), a dramatic [decline in U.S. crime rates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crime_in_the_United_States#Crime_over_time "Crime in the United States"), and [advances in technology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technological_and_industrial_history_of_the_United_States#Computers_and_information_networks "Technological and industrial history of the United States"). Throughout this decade, technological innovations such as the [World Wide Web](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Wide_Web "World Wide Web"), the evolution of the [Pentium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pentium_(original) "Pentium (original)") microprocessor in accordance with [Moore's law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moore%27s_law "Moore's law"), rechargeable [lithium-ion batteries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithium-ion_battery "Lithium-ion battery"), the first [gene therapy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gene_therapy "Gene therapy") trial, and [cloning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cloning "Cloning") either emerged in the U.S. or were improved upon there. The [Human Genome Project](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_Genome_Project "Human Genome Project") was formally launched in 1990, while [Nasdaq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nasdaq "Nasdaq") became the first stock market in the United States to trade online in 1998.[[174]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-191)

In the [Gulf War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_War "Gulf War") of 1991, [an American-led international coalition of states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coalition_of_the_Gulf_War "Coalition of the Gulf War") expelled an [Iraqi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ba%27athist_Iraq "Ba'athist Iraq") invasion force that had occupied neighboring [Kuwait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait "Kuwait").[[175]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-192) The [September 11 attacks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/September_11_attacks "September 11 attacks") on the United States in 2001 by the [pan-Islamist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pan-Islamism "Pan-Islamism") militant organization [al-Qaeda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Qaeda "Al-Qaeda") led to the [war on terror](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_on_terror "War on terror") and subsequent [military interventions in Afghanistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%932021) "War in Afghanistan (2001â€“2021)") and [in Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq_War "Iraq War").[[176]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-193)[[177]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-194)

The [U.S. housing bubble](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2000s_United_States_housing_bubble "2000s United States housing bubble") culminated in 2007 with the [Great Recession](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Recession "Great Recession"), the largest economic contraction since the Great Depression.[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-195) In the 2010s and early 2020s, the United States has experienced increased [political polarization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_polarization_in_the_United_States "Political polarization in the United States") and [democratic backsliding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_backsliding_in_the_United_States "Democratic backsliding in the United States").[[179]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-196)[[180]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-197)[[181]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-198)[[182]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-199) The country's polarization was violently reflected in the [January 2021 Capitol attack](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/January_6_United_States_Capitol_attack "January 6 United States Capitol attack"),[[183]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Kleinfeld-2023-200) when a mob of insurrectionists[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Pape-2022-201) entered the [U.S. Capitol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Capitol "United States Capitol") and sought to prevent the peaceful transfer of power[[185]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-202) in an [attempted self-coup d'Ã©tat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-coup#Notable_events_described_as_attempted_self-coups "Self-coup").[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Multiple_Sources-203)

Geography
---------

Main article: [Geography of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geography_of_the_United_States "Geography of the United States")

[![Image 35](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Uspaintedrelief.png/250px-Uspaintedrelief.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Uspaintedrelief.png)

A [topographic map](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Topographic_map "Topographic map") of the United States

The United States is the world's [third-largest country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area "List of countries and dependencies by area") by total area behind Russia and Canada.[[c]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-largestcountry-15) The 48 [contiguous states and the District of Columbia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contiguous_United_States "Contiguous United States") have a combined area of 3,119,885 square miles (8,080,470 km 2).[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-CensusGov2010HTML-14)[[187]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-204) In 2021, the United States had 8% of the Earth's permanent meadows and pastures and 10% of its cropland.[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Food_and_Agriculture_Organization_of_the_United_Nations-2023-205)

Starting in the east, [the coastal plain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlantic_Plain "Atlantic Plain") of the [Atlantic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean "Atlantic Ocean") seaboard gives way to inland forests and rolling hills in the [Piedmont](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Piedmont_(United_States) "Piedmont (United States)") plateau region.[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-206) The [Appalachian Mountains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains "Appalachian Mountains") and the [Adirondack Massif](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adirondack_Mountains "Adirondack Mountains") separate the [East Coast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States "East Coast of the United States") from the [Great Lakes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Lakes "Great Lakes") and the grasslands of [the Midwest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Midwestern_United_States "Midwestern United States").[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-NAU-207) The [Mississippi River System](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mississippi_River_System "Mississippi River System"), the world's [fourth-longest river system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_rivers_by_length "List of rivers by length"), runs predominantly northâ€“south through the center of the country. The flat and fertile [prairie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prairie "Prairie") of the [Great Plains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Plains "Great Plains") stretches to the west, interrupted by [a highland region](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Interior_Highlands "U.S. Interior Highlands") in the southeast.[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-NAU-207)

[![Image 36](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Canyon_River_Tree_%28165872763%29.jpeg/250px-Canyon_River_Tree_%28165872763%29.jpeg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Canyon_River_Tree_(165872763).jpeg)

The [Grand Canyon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Canyon "Grand Canyon") in Arizona

The [Rocky Mountains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rocky_Mountains "Rocky Mountains"), west of the Great Plains, extend north to south across the country, peaking at over 14,000 feet (4,300 m) in [Colorado](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colorado "Colorado").[[191]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-208) The [supervolcano](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supervolcano "Supervolcano") underlying [Yellowstone National Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yellowstone_National_Park "Yellowstone National Park") in the Rocky Mountains, the [Yellowstone Caldera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yellowstone_Caldera "Yellowstone Caldera"), is the continent's largest volcanic feature.[[192]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-209) Farther west are the rocky [Great Basin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Basin "Great Basin") and the [Chihuahuan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chihuahuan_Desert "Chihuahuan Desert"), [Sonoran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sonoran_Desert "Sonoran Desert"), and [Mojave](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mojave_Desert "Mojave Desert") deserts.[[193]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-210) In the northwest corner of [Arizona](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arizona "Arizona"), carved by the [Colorado River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colorado_River "Colorado River"), is the [Grand Canyon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Canyon "Grand Canyon"), a steep-sided canyon and popular tourist destination[[194]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-211) known for its overwhelming visual size and intricate, colorful landscape. The [Cascade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cascade_Range "Cascade Range") and [Sierra Nevada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sierra_Nevada "Sierra Nevada") mountain ranges run close to the [Pacific coast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Coast_of_the_United_States "West Coast of the United States"). The [lowest and highest points in the contiguous United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extreme_points_of_the_United_States "Extreme points of the United States") are in the State of California,[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-212) about 84 miles (135 km) apart.[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-213)

At an elevation of 20,310 feet (6,190.5 m), Alaska's [Denali](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denali "Denali") (also called Mount McKinley) is the highest peak in the country and on the continent.[[197]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-214) Active [volcanoes in the U.S.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_volcanoes_in_the_United_States "List of volcanoes in the United States") are common throughout Alaska's [Alexander](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_Archipelago "Alexander Archipelago") and [Aleutian Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aleutian_Islands "Aleutian Islands"). Located entirely outside North America, the archipelago of Hawaii consists of volcanic islands, [physiographically](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physical_geography "Physical geography") and [ethnologically](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnology "Ethnology") part of the [Polynesian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polynesia "Polynesia") subregion of [Oceania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oceania "Oceania").[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-215)

In addition to its total land area, the United States has one of the world's largest marine [exclusive economic zones](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exclusive_economic_zones "Exclusive economic zones") spanning approximately 4.5 million square miles (11.7 million km 2) of ocean.[[199]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-216)[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-217)

### Climate

Main article: [Climate of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_of_the_United_States "Climate of the United States")

[![Image 37](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Types_US_50.png/250px-K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Types_US_50.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Types_US_50.png)

The [KÃ¶ppen climate types](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification "KÃ¶ppen climate classification") of the United States

With its large size and geographic variety, the United States includes most climate types. East of the [100th meridian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/100th_meridian_west "100th meridian west"), the climate ranges from [humid continental](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humid_continental_climate "Humid continental climate") in the north to [humid subtropical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate "Humid subtropical climate") in the south.[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-218) The western Great Plains are [semi-arid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semi-arid_climate "Semi-arid climate").[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-219) Many mountainous areas of the American West have an [alpine climate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alpine_climate "Alpine climate"). The climate is [arid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desert_climate "Desert climate") in the Southwest, [Mediterranean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mediterranean_climate "Mediterranean climate") in [coastal California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coastal_California "Coastal California"), and [oceanic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oceanic_climate "Oceanic climate") in coastal [Oregon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oregon "Oregon"), [Washington](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington_(state) "Washington (state)"), and southern [Alaska](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alaska "Alaska"). Most of Alaska is [subarctic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subarctic_climate "Subarctic climate") or [polar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polar_climate "Polar climate"). [Hawaii](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hawaii "Hawaii"), the [southern tip of Florida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Florida "South Florida") and U.S. territories in the [Caribbean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caribbean "Caribbean") and [Pacific](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pacific_Ocean "Pacific Ocean") are [tropical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_climate "Tropical climate").[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-220)

The United States receives more high-impact [extreme weather](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extreme_weather "Extreme weather") incidents than any other country.[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-221)[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-222) States bordering the [Gulf of Mexico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico "Gulf of Mexico") are prone to hurricanes, and most of the world's tornadoes [occur in the country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tornadoes_in_the_United_States "Tornadoes in the United States"), mainly in [Tornado Alley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tornado_Alley "Tornado Alley").[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-223) Due to [climate change in the country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change_in_the_United_States "Climate change in the United States"), extreme weather has become more frequent in the U.S. in the 21st century, with three times the number of reported [heat waves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heat_waves "Heat waves") compared to the 1960s.[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-224)[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-225)[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-226) Since the 1990s, droughts in the [American Southwest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southwestern_United_States "Southwestern United States") have become more persistent and more severe.[[210]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-227) The regions considered as the most attractive to the population are the most vulnerable.[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-228)

### Biodiversity and conservation

Main articles: [Fauna of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fauna_of_the_United_States "Fauna of the United States") and [Flora of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flora_of_the_United_States "Flora of the United States")

[![Image 38: A bald eagle](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Bald_eagle_about_to_fly_in_Alaska_%282016%29.jpg/250px-Bald_eagle_about_to_fly_in_Alaska_%282016%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bald_eagle_about_to_fly_in_Alaska_(2016).jpg)

The [bald eagle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bald_eagle "Bald eagle"), the [national emblem of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bald_eagle#National_symbol_of_the_United_States "Bald eagle") since 1782 and officially declared the national bird in 2024[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-229)

The U.S. is one of 17 [megadiverse countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Megadiverse_countries "Megadiverse countries") containing large numbers of [endemic species](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_endangered_animals_of_North_America "List of endangered animals of North America"): about 17,000 species of [vascular plants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vascular_plant "Vascular plant") occur in the contiguous United States and Alaska, and over 1,800 species of [flowering plants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flowering_plant "Flowering plant") are found in Hawaii, few of which occur on the mainland.[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-230) The United States is home to 428 [mammal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mammal "Mammal") species, 784 birds, 311 reptiles, 295 [amphibians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amphibian "Amphibian"),[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Current_Results_#_of_native_species_in_the_US-231) and around 91,000 insect species.[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-232)

There are [63 national parks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_national_parks_of_the_United_States "List of national parks of the United States"), and [hundreds of other federally managed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_lands "Federal lands") monuments, forests, and [wilderness areas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Wilderness_Preservation_System "National Wilderness Preservation System"), administered by the [National Park Service](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Park_Service "National Park Service") and other agencies.[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-233) About 28% of the country's land is publicly owned and federally managed,[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-NYTimes_Federal_Land-234) primarily in the [Western States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_United_States "Western United States").[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-AKLeg_CRS_Federal_Land-235)[Most of this land is protected](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protected_areas_of_the_United_States "Protected areas of the United States"), though some is leased for commercial use, and less than one percent is used for military purposes.[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Federal_Land_Ownership-236)[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Fed_Land_Uses-237)

[Environmental issues in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environmental_issues_in_the_United_States "Environmental issues in the United States") include debates on [non-renewable resources](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-renewable_resource "Non-renewable resource") and [nuclear energy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_power_debate "Nuclear power debate"), [air and water pollution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pollution_prevention_in_the_US "Pollution prevention in the US"), [biodiversity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biodiversity "Biodiversity"), logging and [deforestation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deforestation_in_the_United_States "Deforestation in the United States"),[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-238)[[222]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-239) and [climate change](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change_in_the_United_States "Climate change in the United States").[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-240)[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-241) The [U.S. Environmental Protection Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency "United States Environmental Protection Agency") (EPA) is the federal agency charged with [addressing most environmental-related issues](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environmental_policy_of_the_United_States "Environmental policy of the United States").[[225]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Collin2006-242) The [idea of wilderness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Wilderness_Preservation_System "National Wilderness Preservation System") has shaped the management of public lands since 1964, with the [Wilderness Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilderness_Act "Wilderness Act").[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-243) The [Endangered Species Act of 1973](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endangered_Species_Act_of_1973 "Endangered Species Act of 1973") provides a way to protect threatened and endangered species and their habitats. The [United States Fish and Wildlife Service](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Fish_and_Wildlife_Service "United States Fish and Wildlife Service") implements and enforces the Act.[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Office-244) In 2024, the U.S. ranked 35th among 180 countries in the [Environmental Performance Index](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environmental_Performance_Index "Environmental Performance Index").[[228]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-245)

Government and politics
-----------------------

Main article: [Politics of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Politics_of_the_United_States "Politics of the United States")

[![Image 39](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/United_States_Capitol_west_front_edit2.jpg/250px-United_States_Capitol_west_front_edit2.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:United_States_Capitol_west_front_edit2.jpg)

The [Capitol Building](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Capitol "United States Capitol"), seat of legislative government, houses both chambers of [Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Congress "U.S. Congress").

[![Image 40](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/White_House_lawn_%28long_tightly_cropped%29.jpg/250px-White_House_lawn_%28long_tightly_cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:White_House_lawn_(long_tightly_cropped).jpg)

The [White House](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_House "White House"), residence and workplace of the president, includes offices for [the executive staff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_Office_of_the_President_of_the_United_States "Executive Office of the President of the United States").

[![Image 41](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Panorama_of_United_States_Supreme_Court_Building_at_Dusk.jpg/250px-Panorama_of_United_States_Supreme_Court_Building_at_Dusk.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Panorama_of_United_States_Supreme_Court_Building_at_Dusk.jpg)

The [Supreme Court Building](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Supreme_Court_Building "United States Supreme Court Building") houses the [nation's highest court](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States "Supreme Court of the United States").

The United States is a [federal republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_republic "Federal republic") of 50 [states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._state "U.S. state") and a federal capital district, [Washington, D.C.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington,_D.C. "Washington, D.C.") The U.S. asserts sovereignty over five [unincorporated territories](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States "Territories of the United States") and [several uninhabited island possessions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Minor_Outlying_Islands "United States Minor Outlying Islands").[[19]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-HRI-2012-28)[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOnuf2010xvii-246) It is the world's oldest surviving federation,[[230]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-247) and its [presidential system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidential_system "Presidential system") of national government has been adopted, in whole or in part, by many newly independent states worldwide following their [decolonization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decolonization "Decolonization").[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-248) The [Constitution of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_the_United_States "Constitution of the United States") serves as [the country's supreme legal document](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supremacy_Clause "Supremacy Clause").[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-249) Most scholars describe the United States as a [liberal democracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberal_democracy "Liberal democracy").[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Scheb-250)[[r]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-262)

### Federal government

Main article: [Federal government of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States "Federal government of the United States")

Composed of three branches, all headquartered in Washington, D.C., the federal government is the national government of the United States. The [U.S. Constitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Constitution "U.S. Constitution") establishes a [separation of powers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Separation_of_powers "Separation of powers") intended to provide a system of [checks and balances](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Checks_and_balances "Checks and balances") to prevent any of the three branches from becoming supreme.[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-263)

*   The [U.S. Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Congress "United States Congress") is a [bicameral legislature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bicameral_legislature "Bicameral legislature") made up of the [Senate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Senate "United States Senate") and the [House of Representatives](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives "United States House of Representatives"). The Senate has 100 membersâ€”two residents from each state and elected by that state's voters for a six-year term. The House of Representatives has 435 members, elected for a two-year term by the constituency of the [congressional district](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_United_States_congressional_districts "List of United States congressional districts") where they reside. A [state's legislature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_legislature_(United_States) "State legislature (United States)") decides the district boundaries, which are contiguous within the state. Every U.S. congressional district is of equivalent population and sends one representative to Congress.[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-264) Election years for senators are staggered so that only one-third of them will be up for election every two years.[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-265) U.S. representatives are all up for election at the same time every two years. The U.S. Congress makes [federal law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_law "Federal law"), [declares war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Declaration_of_war "Declaration of war"), approves treaties, has the [power of the purse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Power_of_the_purse "Power of the purse"),[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-266) and has [the power of impeachment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Impeachment_in_the_United_States "Impeachment in the United States").[[249]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-267) One of its foremost non-legislative functions is [the power to investigate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congressional_investigation "Congressional investigation") and oversee the executive branch.[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-tws2010Sep11t11-268)[Congressional oversight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congressional_oversight "Congressional oversight") is usually delegated to committees and is facilitated by [Congress's power to issue subpoenas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contempt_of_Congress "Contempt of Congress").[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-tws2010Sep11t13-269) Much of the work of Congress is performed by [a collection of committees](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_congressional_committee "United States congressional committee"), each appointed for a specific purpose or function. Committee membership is by tradition and statute [bipartisan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bipartisan "Bipartisan"), but all committees are [chaired](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chair_(officer) "Chair (officer)") by a member of the [majority party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Majority_party "Majority party"), who sets the committee agenda.[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-270)

[![Image 42](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Official_Presidential_Portrait_of_President_Donald_J._Trump_%282025%29.jpg/250px-Official_Presidential_Portrait_of_President_Donald_J._Trump_%282025%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Official_Presidential_Portrait_of_President_Donald_J._Trump_(2025).jpg)

[Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump "Donald Trump")

[President](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_the_United_States "President of the United States")

[![Image 43](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/January_2025_Official_Vice_Presidential_Portrait_of_JD_Vance.jpg/250px-January_2025_Official_Vice_Presidential_Portrait_of_JD_Vance.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:January_2025_Official_Vice_Presidential_Portrait_of_JD_Vance.jpg)

[JD Vance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/JD_Vance "JD Vance")

[Vice President](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States "Vice President of the United States")

*   The U.S. president is the [head of state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Head_of_state "Head of state"), [commander-in-chief](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commander-in-chief "Commander-in-chief") of the military, [chief executive of the federal government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Head_of_government "Head of government"), and has the ability to veto [legislative bills](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_(law) "Bill (law)") from the U.S. Congress before they become law. However, [presidential vetoes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Veto_power_in_the_United_States "Veto power in the United States") can be overridden by a two-thirds [supermajority](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supermajority#Use_in_governments_around_the_world "Supermajority") vote in both chambers of Congress. The president appoints the [members of the Cabinet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_United_States "Cabinet of the United States"), subject to Senate approval, and names other officials who administer and enforce federal law and policy through [their respective agencies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_federal_agencies_in_the_United_States "List of federal agencies in the United States").[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-271) The president also has clemency power for federal crimes and [can issue pardons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_pardons_in_the_United_States "Federal pardons in the United States"). Finally, the president has the authority to issue expansive "[executive orders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_orders "Executive orders")" in a number of policy areas, subject to [judicial review](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judicial_review_in_the_United_States "Judicial review in the United States"). Candidates for president campaign with a vice-presidential [running mate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Running_mate "Running mate"). Both candidates are elected together, or defeated together, in a presidential election. Unlike other votes in American politics, this is technically an [indirect election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indirect_election "Indirect election") in which the winner will be determined by the [U.S. Electoral College](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Electoral_College "United States Electoral College"). There, votes are officially cast by individual electors selected by [their state legislature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_legislature_(United_States) "State legislature (United States)").[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-272) In practice, however, each of the 50 states chooses a group of presidential electors who are required by state law to confirm the winner of their state's popular vote. Each state is allocated two electors plus one additional elector for every congressional district in the state, which in effect combines to equal the number of elected officials that state sends to Congress. The District of Columbia, with no representatives or senators, is allocated three electoral votes. Both the president and the vice president serve a four-year term, and the president may be [reelected to the office only once](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twenty-second_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution "Twenty-second Amendment to the United States Constitution"), for one additional four-year term.[[s]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-273)
*   The [U.S. federal judiciary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_judiciary_of_the_United_States "Federal judiciary of the United States"), whose judges are all appointed for life by the president with Senate approval, consists primarily of the [U.S. Supreme Court](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States "Supreme Court of the United States"), the [U.S. courts of appeals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_courts_of_appeals "United States courts of appeals"), and the [U.S. district courts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_district_court "United States district court"). The lowest level in the federal judiciary is the federal district court, which decides all cases considered to be under "[original jurisdiction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Original_jurisdiction#Federal_and_state_courts "Original jurisdiction")", such as federal statutes, constitutional law, or [international treaties](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_treaties "International treaties"). After a federal district court has decided a case, its decision may be contested and sent to a higher court, a federal court of appeals. The U.S. judicial system's 12 federal circuits divide the country into 12 separate geographic administrative regions for appeals decisions. The next and highest court in the system is the Supreme Court of the United States.[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FedJud-274) The U.S. Supreme Court interprets laws and [overturns those it finds unconstitutional](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judicial_review "Judicial review").[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FedJud-274) On average, the Supreme Court receives about 7,000 appeals petitions for [writs of certiorari](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Writs_of_certiorari "Writs of certiorari") each year, but only grants about 80.[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-275) Consisting of nine members led by the [Chief Justice of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_the_United_States "Chief Justice of the United States"), the court judges each case before it by majority decision. As with all other federal judges, the members are appointed for life by the sitting president with Senate approval when a vacancy becomes available.[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-276)

The three-branch system is known as the [presidential system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidential_system "Presidential system"), in contrast to the [parliamentary system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliamentary_system "Parliamentary system") where the executive is part of the legislative body. Many countries around the world adopted this aspect of the 1789 Constitution of the United States, especially in the [postcolonial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Postcolonialism "Postcolonialism") Americas.[[258]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Sundquist-277)

### Subdivisions

Main articles: [U.S. state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._state "U.S. state"), [County (United States)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/County_(United_States) "County (United States)"), [Indian country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_country "Indian country"), and [Territories of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States "Territories of the United States")

Further information: [List of states and territories of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_states_and_territories_of_the_United_States "List of states and territories of the United States"), [List of federally recognized tribes by state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_federally_recognized_tribes_by_state "List of federally recognized tribes by state"), and [Federally recognized tribe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federally_recognized_tribe "Federally recognized tribe")

[![Image 44: Territories of the United States.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/United_States_%28%2Boverseas%29%2C_administrative_divisions_-_en_-_colored_%28zoom%29.svg/330px-United_States_%28%2Boverseas%29%2C_administrative_divisions_-_en_-_colored_%28zoom%29.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:United_States_(%2Boverseas),_administrative_divisions_-_en_-_colored_(zoom).svg)

[Territories of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States "Territories of the United States") include [American Samoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Samoa "American Samoa"), [Guam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guam "Guam"), the [Northern Mariana Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands "Northern Mariana Islands"), [Puerto Rico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puerto_Rico "Puerto Rico"), and the [U.S. Virgin Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands "United States Virgin Islands").

In the [U.S. federal system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federalism_in_the_United_States "Federalism in the United States"), sovereign powers are shared between three levels of government specified in the Constitution: the national government, the states, and Indian tribes.[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-3Sovereigns-278)[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FelixSCohen-279) The U.S. also asserts sovereignty over five permanently inhabited territories: [American Samoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Samoa "American Samoa"), [Guam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guam "Guam"), the [Northern Mariana Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands "Northern Mariana Islands"), [Puerto Rico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puerto_Rico "Puerto Rico"), and the [U.S. Virgin Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands "United States Virgin Islands").[[19]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-HRI-2012-28)

Residents of the 50 states are governed by their elected state government, under [state constitutions compatible with the national constitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_constitutions_in_the_United_States "State constitutions in the United States"), and by elected [local governments](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Local_government_in_the_United_States "Local government in the United States") that are administrative divisions of a state.[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-280) States are subdivided into counties or county equivalents, and (except for Hawaii) [further divided into municipalities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Local_government_in_the_United_States "Local government in the United States"), each administered by elected representatives. The District of Columbia is [a federal district](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_district_of_the_United_States "Federal district of the United States") containing the U.S. capital, [Washington, D.C.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington,_D.C. "Washington, D.C.")[[262]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-281) The federal district is an administrative division of the federal government.[[263]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-282)

[![Image 45](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Indian_Reservations.png/250px-Indian_Reservations.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Indian_Reservations.png)

Map of [326 Indian reservations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Indian_reservations_in_the_United_States "List of Indian reservations in the United States") in the United States; 231 recognized [Alaska Native tribes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Alaska_Native_tribal_entities "List of Alaska Native tribal entities") are not shown.

Indian country is made up of 574 [federally recognized tribes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federally_recognized_tribe "Federally recognized tribe") and [326 Indian reservations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Indian_reservations_in_the_United_States "List of Indian reservations in the United States"). They hold a government-to-government relationship with the U.S. federal government in Washington and are legally defined as [domestic dependent nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domestic_dependent_nations "Domestic dependent nations") with [inherent tribal sovereignty rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tribal_sovereignty_in_the_United_States "Tribal sovereignty in the United States").[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FelixSCohen-279)[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-3Sovereigns-278)[[264]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-283)[[265]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-www.justice.gov-2017-284)

In addition to the five major territories, the U.S. also asserts sovereignty over the [United States Minor Outlying Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Minor_Outlying_Islands "United States Minor Outlying Islands") in the [Pacific Ocean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pacific_Ocean "Pacific Ocean") and the [Caribbean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caribbean "Caribbean").[[19]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-HRI-2012-28) The seven undisputed islands without permanent populations are [Baker Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baker_Island "Baker Island"), [Howland Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Howland_Island "Howland Island"), [Jarvis Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jarvis_Island "Jarvis Island"), [Johnston Atoll](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johnston_Atoll "Johnston Atoll"), [Kingman Reef](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingman_Reef "Kingman Reef"), [Midway Atoll](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Midway_Atoll "Midway Atoll"), and [Palmyra Atoll](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palmyra_Atoll "Palmyra Atoll"). U.S. sovereignty over the unpopulated [Bajo Nuevo Bank](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bajo_Nuevo_Bank "Bajo Nuevo Bank"), [Navassa Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Navassa_Island "Navassa Island"), [Serranilla Bank](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serranilla_Bank "Serranilla Bank"), and [Wake Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wake_Island "Wake Island") is disputed.[[19]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-HRI-2012-28)

![Image 46](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Map_of_USA_with_state_and_territory_names_2.png/960px-Map_of_USA_with_state_and_territory_names_2.png)[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Map_of_USA_with_state_and_territory_names_2.png)

### Political parties

Main article: [Political parties in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_parties_in_the_United_States "Political parties in the United States")

Further information: [List of political parties in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_the_United_States "List of political parties in the United States") and [Political party strength in U.S. states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_party_strength_in_U.S._states "Political party strength in U.S. states")

[![Image 47](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/US_state_Legislature_and_Governor_Control.svg/250px-US_state_Legislature_and_Governor_Control.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:US_state_Legislature_and_Governor_Control.svg)

States and territories by partisan control, as of February 2025: 

[Democratic Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States) "Democratic Party (United States)")

[Republican Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States) "Republican Party (United States)")

[New Progressive Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Progressive_Party_(Puerto_Rico) "New Progressive Party (Puerto Rico)")

Divided partisan control

The Constitution is silent on political parties. However, they developed independently in the 18th century with the [Federalist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federalist_Party "Federalist Party") and [Anti-Federalist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Federalist_Party "Anti-Federalist Party") parties.[[266]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Hofstadter-1969-iv-285) Since then, the United States has operated as a _de facto_[two-party system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Two-party_system "Two-party system"), though the parties have changed over time.[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Blake-2021-286) Since the mid-19th century, the two main national parties have been the [Democratic Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States) "Democratic Party (United States)") and the [Republican Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States) "Republican Party (United States)"). The former is perceived as [relatively liberal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_liberalism_in_the_United_States "Modern liberalism in the United States") in [its political platform](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_positions_of_the_Democratic_Party_(United_States) "Political positions of the Democratic Party (United States)") while the latter is perceived as [relatively conservative](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conservatism_in_the_United_States "Conservatism in the United States") in [its platform](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_positions_of_the_Republican_Party_(United_States) "Political positions of the Republican Party (United States)").[[268]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-287)

### Foreign relations

Main articles: [Foreign relations of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_United_States "Foreign relations of the United States") and [Foreign policy of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_policy_of_the_United_States "Foreign policy of the United States")

[![Image 48: see caption](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Midtown_Manhattan_Skyline_004_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Midtown_Manhattan_Skyline_004_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Midtown_Manhattan_Skyline_004_(cropped).jpg)

The [United Nations headquarters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Headquarters_of_the_United_Nations "Headquarters of the United Nations") has been situated along the [East River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_River "East River") in [Midtown Manhattan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Midtown_Manhattan "Midtown Manhattan") since 1952; in 1945, the United States was a [founding member of the UN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Founding_member_of_the_United_Nations "Founding member of the United Nations").

The United States has an established structure of foreign relations, with the world's [second-largest diplomatic corps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_diplomatic_missions "List of countries by number of diplomatic missions") as of 2024[[update]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=United_States&action=edit). It is a [permanent member of the United Nations Security Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permanent_members_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council "Permanent members of the United Nations Security Council")[[269]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-288) and home to the [United Nations headquarters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Headquarters_of_the_United_Nations "Headquarters of the United Nations").[[270]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-289) The United States is a member of the [G7](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G7 "G7"),[[271]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-290)[G20](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G20 "G20"),[[272]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-291) and [OECD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OECD "OECD") intergovernmental organizations.[[273]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-292)[Almost all countries have embassies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_in_the_United_States "List of diplomatic missions in the United States") and many have [consulates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consul_(representative) "Consul (representative)") (official representatives) in the country. Likewise, nearly all countries host formal [diplomatic missions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diplomatic_mission "Diplomatic mission") with the United States, except [Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Iranâ€“United States relations"),[[274]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-293)[North Korea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Korea%E2%80%93United_States_relations "North Koreaâ€“United States relations"),[[275]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-294) and [Bhutan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Bhutan#Other_countries "Foreign relations of Bhutan").[[276]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-295) Though [Taiwan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiwan%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Taiwanâ€“United States relations") does not have formal diplomatic relations with the U.S., it maintains close unofficial relations.[[277]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-296) The United States regularly [supplies Taiwan with military equipment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Six_Assurances "Six Assurances") to deter potential Chinese aggression.[[278]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-297) Its geopolitical attention also turned to the [Indo-Pacific](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Pacific "Indo-Pacific") when the United States joined the [Quadrilateral Security Dialogue](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quadrilateral_Security_Dialogue "Quadrilateral Security Dialogue") with Australia, India, and Japan.[[279]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-kobara-298)

The United States has a "[Special Relationship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special_Relationship "Special Relationship")" [with the United Kingdom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom%E2%80%93United_States_relations "United Kingdomâ€“United States relations")[[280]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-299) and strong ties [with Canada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Canadaâ€“United States relations"),[[281]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-300)[Australia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Australia%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Australiaâ€“United States relations"),[[282]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-301)[New Zealand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Zealand%E2%80%93United_States_relations "New Zealandâ€“United States relations"),[[283]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-302)[the Philippines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippines%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Philippinesâ€“United States relations"),[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-303)[Japan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japan%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Japanâ€“United States relations"),[[285]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-304)[South Korea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Korea%E2%80%93United_States_relations "South Koreaâ€“United States relations"),[[286]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-305)[Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Israelâ€“United States relations"),[[287]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-306) and several [European Union countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union "Member state of the European Union") such as [France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/France%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Franceâ€“United States relations"), [Italy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italy%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Italyâ€“United States relations"), [Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germany%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Germanyâ€“United States relations"), [Spain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spain%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Spainâ€“United States relations"), and [Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poland%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Polandâ€“United States relations").[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-307) The U.S. works closely with its [NATO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NATO "NATO") allies on military and [national security](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_security "National security") issues, and with countries in the Americas through the [Organization of American States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organization_of_American_States "Organization of American States") and the [United Statesâ€“Mexicoâ€“Canada Free Trade Agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States%E2%80%93Mexico%E2%80%93Canada_Agreement "United Statesâ€“Mexicoâ€“Canada Agreement"). The U.S. exercises full international defense authority and responsibility for [Micronesia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federated_States_of_Micronesia "Federated States of Micronesia"), the [Marshall Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marshall_Islands "Marshall Islands"), and [Palau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palau "Palau") through the [Compact of Free Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compact_of_Free_Association "Compact of Free Association").[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FedJud-274) It has increasingly conducted strategic cooperation [with India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Indiaâ€“United States relations"),[[289]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-308) while [its ties with China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Chinaâ€“United States relations") have steadily deteriorated.[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-309)[[291]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-310)

Beginning in 2014, the U.S. had become [a key ally of Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukraine%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Ukraineâ€“United States relations").[[292]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-311)[[293]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-312) After [Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump "Donald Trump") was elected U.S. president in 2024, he sought to negotiate an end to the [Russo-Ukrainian War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Ukrainian_War "Russo-Ukrainian War"). He paused all military aid to Ukraine in March 2025,[[294]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-313) although the aid resumed later.[[295]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-314) Trump also ended U.S. intelligence sharing with the country,[[296]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-:5-315) but this too was eventually restored.[[297]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-316)

### Military

Main article: [United States Armed Forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces "United States Armed Forces")

[![Image 49](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/The_Pentagon%2C_Headquarters_of_the_US_Department_of_Defense_%28cropped2%29.jpg/250px-The_Pentagon%2C_Headquarters_of_the_US_Department_of_Defense_%28cropped2%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_Pentagon,_Headquarters_of_the_US_Department_of_Defense_(cropped2).jpg)

[The Pentagon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Pentagon "The Pentagon"), the headquarters of the [U.S. Department of Defense](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense "United States Department of Defense") in [Arlington County, Virginia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arlington_County,_Virginia "Arlington County, Virginia"), is one of the world's largest office buildings with over 6.5 million square feet (600,000 m 2) of [floor space](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Floor_space "Floor space").

The president is the [commander-in-chief](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commander-in-Chief_of_the_United_States "Commander-in-Chief of the United States") of the United States Armed Forces and appoints its leaders, the [secretary of defense](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Defense "United States Secretary of Defense") and the [Joint Chiefs of Staff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_Chiefs_of_Staff "Joint Chiefs of Staff"). The [Department of Defense](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense "United States Department of Defense"), headquartered at [the Pentagon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Pentagon "The Pentagon") near Washington, D.C., administers five of the six service branches, which are made up of the [U.S. Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Army "United States Army"), [Marine Corps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps "United States Marine Corps"), [Navy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Navy "United States Navy"), [Air Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Air_Force "United States Air Force"), and [Space Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Space_Force "United States Space Force").[[298]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-317) The [Coast Guard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard "United States Coast Guard") is administered by the [Department of Homeland Security](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Homeland_Security "United States Department of Homeland Security") in peacetime and can be transferred to the [Department of the Navy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Navy "United States Department of the Navy") in wartime.[[299]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-318)

The United States [spent $997 billion on its military](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_budget_of_the_United_States "Military budget of the United States") in 2024, which is by far the [largest amount of any country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_with_highest_military_expenditures "List of countries with highest military expenditures"), making up 37% of global military spending and accounting for 3.4% of the country's GDP._**[[300]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United\_States#cite\_note-SIPRI-20202-319)**_ The [U.S. possesses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_weapons_of_the_United_States "Nuclear weapons of the United States") 42% of the world's nuclear weaponsâ€”the second-largest stockpile after [that of Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction "Russia and weapons of mass destruction").[[301]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Stockholm_International_Peace_Research_Institute-2024-320) The U.S. military is widely regarded as the most powerful and advanced in the world.[[302]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-321)[[303]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-322)

The United States has the [third-largest combined armed forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_military_and_paramilitary_personnel "List of countries by number of military and paramilitary personnel") in the world, behind the [Chinese People's Liberation Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army "People's Liberation Army") and [Indian Armed Forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Armed_Forces "Indian Armed Forces").[[304]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-323) The U.S. military operates about 800 bases and facilities abroad,[[305]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-324) and maintains [deployments greater than 100 active duty personnel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_military_deployments "United States military deployments") in 25 foreign countries.[[306]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-325) The United States has engaged in over 400 military interventions since its founding in 1776, with over half of these occurring between 1950 and 2019 and 25% occurring in the post-Cold War era.[[307]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-326)

[State defense forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_defense_forces "State defense forces") (SDFs) are military units that operate under the sole authority of a state government. SDFs are authorized by state and federal law but are under the command of [the state's governor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Governor_(United_States) "Governor (United States)").[[308]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-327)[[309]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-328)[[310]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-329) By contrast, a state's [National Guard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Guard_(United_States) "National Guard (United States)") units are under the dual control of [state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_governments_of_the_United_States "State governments of the United States") and [federal governments](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States "Federal government of the United States"); such units can also become federalized entities, but SDFs cannot be federalized.[[311]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-330) A state's National Guard personnel can be federalized by the president under the [National Defense Act Amendments of 1933](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Defense_Act_of_1916#National_Defense_Act_Amendments_of_1933 "National Defense Act of 1916"), which created the Guard and provides for the integration of [Army National Guard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Army_National_Guard "Army National Guard")&[Air National Guard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Air_National_Guard "Air National Guard") units and personnel into the U.S. Army and (since 1947) the U.S. Air Force.[[312]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-331)

### Law enforcement and criminal justice

Main articles: [Law of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_of_the_United_States "Law of the United States"), [Law enforcement in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_the_United_States "Law enforcement in the United States"), and [Crime in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crime_in_the_United_States "Crime in the United States")

[![Image 50](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/FBI_Headquarters_-_J._Edgar_Hoover_Building_%2853840035941%29.jpg/250px-FBI_Headquarters_-_J._Edgar_Hoover_Building_%2853840035941%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:FBI_Headquarters_-_J._Edgar_Hoover_Building_(53840035941).jpg)

[J. Edgar Hoover Building](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._Edgar_Hoover_Building "J. Edgar Hoover Building"), the headquarters of the [Federal Bureau of Investigation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation "Federal Bureau of Investigation") (FBI), in [Washington, D.C.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington,_D.C. "Washington, D.C.")

There are about 18,000 U.S. police agencies from local to national level in the United States.[[313]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-332) Law in the United States is mainly enforced by local police departments and [sheriff departments](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sheriffs_in_the_United_States "Sheriffs in the United States") in their municipal or county jurisdictions. [The state police](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_police_(United_States) "State police (United States)") departments [have authority in their respective state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Police_power_(United_States_constitutional_law) "Police power (United States constitutional law)"), and [federal agencies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_law_enforcement_in_the_United_States "Federal law enforcement in the United States") such as the [Federal Bureau of Investigation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation "Federal Bureau of Investigation") (FBI) and the [U.S. Marshals Service](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Marshals_Service "United States Marshals Service") have national jurisdiction and specialized duties, such as protecting [civil rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_rights "Civil rights"), [national security](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_security_of_the_United_States "National security of the United States"), enforcing [U.S. federal courts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._federal_courts "U.S. federal courts")' rulings and federal laws, and interstate criminal activity.[[314]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-333)[State courts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_court_(United_States) "State court (United States)") conduct almost all civil and criminal trials,[[315]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-334) while federal courts [adjudicate the much smaller number of civil and criminal cases that relate to federal law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subject-matter_jurisdiction "Subject-matter jurisdiction").[[316]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-335)

There is no unified "criminal justice system" in the United States. The [American prison system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Incarceration_in_the_United_States "Incarceration in the United States") is largely heterogenous, with thousands of relatively independent systems operating across federal, state, local, and tribal levels. In 2025, "these systems hold [nearly 2 million people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_incarceration_rate "United States incarceration rate") in 1,566 state prisons, 98 federal prisons, 3,116 local jails, 1,277 juvenile correctional facilities, 133 immigration detention facilities, and 80 Indian country jails, as well as in military prisons, civil commitment centers, state psychiatric hospitals, and prisons in the U.S. territories."[[317]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Sawyer-2025-336)

Despite disparate systems of confinement, four main institutions dominate: [federal prisons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_United_States_federal_prisons "List of United States federal prisons"), [state prisons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lists_of_United_States_state_prisons "Lists of United States state prisons"), local jails, and [juvenile correctional facilities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_juvenile_justice_system "American juvenile justice system").[[318]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-National_Academies_Press-2014-337) Federal prisons are run by the [Federal Bureau of Prisons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Prisons "Federal Bureau of Prisons") and hold pretrial detainees as well as people who have been convicted of federal crimes.[[318]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-National_Academies_Press-2014-337) State prisons, run by the department of corrections of each state, hold people sentenced and serving prison time (usually longer than one year) for felony offenses.[[318]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-National_Academies_Press-2014-337) Local jails are county or municipal facilities that incarcerate defendants prior to trial; they also hold those serving short sentences (typically under a year).[[318]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-National_Academies_Press-2014-337) Juvenile correctional facilities are operated by local or state governments and serve as longer-term placements for any [minor adjudicated as delinquent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juvenile_delinquency "Juvenile delinquency") and ordered by a judge to be confined.[[319]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-338)

In January 2023, the United States had the [sixth-highest per capita incarceration rate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_incarceration_rate "List of countries by incarceration rate") in the worldâ€”531 people per 100,000 inhabitantsâ€”and the largest prison and jail population in the world, with more than 1.9 million people incarcerated.[[317]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Sawyer-2025-336)[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-339)[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-WorldPrisonBrief-340) An analysis of the [World Health Organization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Health_Organization "World Health Organization") Mortality Database from 2010 showed U.S. homicide rates "were 7 times higher than in other high-income countries, driven by [a gun homicide rate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gun_deaths_in_the_United_States "Gun deaths in the United States") that was 25 times higher".[[322]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-341)

Economy
-------

Main article: [Economy of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy_of_the_United_States "Economy of the United States")

[![Image 51: see caption](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/US_one_dollar_bill%2C_obverse%2C_series_2009.jpg/250px-US_one_dollar_bill%2C_obverse%2C_series_2009.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:US_one_dollar_bill,_obverse,_series_2009.jpg)

The [U.S. dollar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_dollar "United States dollar") is the most-used currency [in international transactions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_use_of_the_U.S._dollar "International use of the U.S. dollar") and the world's foremost [reserve currency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reserve_currency "Reserve currency").

The U.S. has a highly developed [mixed economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mixed_economy "Mixed economy")[[323]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-342) that has been the world's largest nominally [since about 1890](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_largest_historical_GDP "List of countries by largest historical GDP").[[324]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-343) Its 2024 [gross domestic product](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gross_domestic_product "Gross domestic product") (GDP)[[e]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-PPP-20) of more than $29 trillion[[325]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-344) constituted over 25% of nominal [global economic output](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gross_world_product "Gross world product"), or 15% at [purchasing power parity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity "Purchasing power parity") (PPP). From 1983 to 2008, U.S. real compounded annual GDP growth was 3.3%, compared to a 2.3% weighted average for the rest of the [G7](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G7 "G7").[[326]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Hagopian-345) The country ranks [first in the world by nominal GDP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal) "List of countries by GDP (nominal)"),[[327]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-346)[second when adjusted for purchasing power parities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP) "List of countries by GDP (PPP)") (PPP),[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-IMFWEO.US-19) and [ninth by PPP-adjusted GDP per capita](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita "List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita").[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-IMFWEO.US-19) In February 2024, the total [U.S. federal government debt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_debt_of_the_United_States "National debt of the United States") was $34.4 trillion.[[328]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-347)

[![Image 52](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/View_of_Empire_State_Building_from_Rockefeller_Center_New_York_City_dllu_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-View_of_Empire_State_Building_from_Rockefeller_Center_New_York_City_dllu_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:View_of_Empire_State_Building_from_Rockefeller_Center_New_York_City_dllu_(cropped).jpg)

[New York City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_City "New York City") is the world's principal [financial center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Financial_center "Financial center"), and [its metropolitan area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_metropolitan_area "New York metropolitan area") is the world's [largest metropolitan economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_cities_by_GDP "List of cities by GDP").

Of the world's [500 largest companies by revenue](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fortune_Global_500 "Fortune Global 500"), [138 were headquartered in the U.S.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_largest_companies_in_the_United_States_by_revenue "List of largest companies in the United States by revenue") in 2025,[[329]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Fortune-2025-348) the highest number of any country.[[330]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-349) The [U.S. dollar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_dollar "United States dollar") is the currency most used [in international transactions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_use_of_the_U.S._dollar "International use of the U.S. dollar") and the world's foremost [reserve currency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reserve_currency "Reserve currency"), backed by the country's dominant economy, [its military](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces "United States Armed Forces"), the [petrodollar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petrodollar "Petrodollar") system, its large [U.S. treasuries market](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Treasury "U.S.
