Treasury"), and its linked [eurodollar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurodollar "Eurodollar").[[331]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-federalreserve.gov-350)[Several countries use it as their official currency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_dollar#Countries_that_use_US_dollar "United States dollar"), and in others it is the [_de facto_ currency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De_facto_currency "De facto currency").[[332]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Benjamin_J._Cohen_2006,_p._17-351)[[333]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-352) The U.S. has [free trade agreements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_trade_agreements "Free trade agreements") with [several countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_trade_agreements_of_the_United_States "Free trade agreements of the United States"), including the [USMCA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States%E2%80%93Mexico%E2%80%93Canada_Agreement "United Statesâ€“Mexicoâ€“Canada Agreement").[[334]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-353) Although the United States has reached a [post-industrial level of economic development](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Post-industrial_economy "Post-industrial economy")[[335]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Collins-2023-354) and is often described as having a [service economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Service_economy "Service economy"),[[335]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Collins-2023-354)[[336]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Econ-355) it remains a major industrial power;[[337]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-356) in 2024, the [U.S. manufacturing sector](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._manufacturing_sector "U.S. manufacturing sector") was the world's [second-largest by value output](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_manufacturing_output "List of countries by manufacturing output") after [China's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manufacturing_in_China "Manufacturing in China").[[338]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-357)

[![Image 53](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Gaming-Wall-Street_BTS_Prodigium-266.jpg/250px-Gaming-Wall-Street_BTS_Prodigium-266.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Gaming-Wall-Street_BTS_Prodigium-266.jpg)

The [New York Stock Exchange](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange "New York Stock Exchange") on [Wall Street](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wall_Street "Wall Street"), the world's [largest stock exchange by market capitalization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_stock_exchanges#Major_stock_exchanges "List of stock exchanges")[[339]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-NYSEhighestcap-358)

[New York City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_City "New York City") is the world's principal [financial center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Financial_center "Financial center"),[[340]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-359)[[341]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-NYCFintechAndFinancialCapitalWorld-360) and [its metropolitan area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_metropolitan_area "New York metropolitan area") is the world's [largest metropolitan economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_cities_by_GDP "List of cities by GDP").[[342]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-NYCEpicenterUSMetroEconomy-361) The [New York Stock Exchange](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange "New York Stock Exchange") and [Nasdaq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nasdaq "Nasdaq"), both located in New York City, are the world's two [largest stock exchanges](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_stock_exchanges "List of stock exchanges") by [market capitalization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Market_capitalization "Market capitalization") and [trade volume](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trade_volume "Trade volume").[[343]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-362)[[344]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-sfc.hk-363) The United States is at the forefront of [technological advancement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_the_United_States "Science and technology in the United States") and [innovation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Innovation "Innovation") in many economic fields, especially in [artificial intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence "Artificial intelligence"); [electronics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electronics "Electronics") and [computers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer "Computer"); [pharmaceuticals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pharmaceuticals "Pharmaceuticals"); and medical, [aerospace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aerospace "Aerospace") and [military equipment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_equipment "Military equipment").[[345]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-CIA-2018-364) The country's economy is fueled by abundant [natural resources](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_resource "Natural resource"), a well-developed [infrastructure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infrastructure_policy_of_the_United_States "Infrastructure policy of the United States"), and [high productivity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_labour_productivity "List of countries by labour productivity").[[346]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Wright,_Gavin_2007_p._185-365) The [largest trading partners of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_the_largest_trading_partners_of_the_United_States "List of the largest trading partners of the United States") are the [European Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union "European Union"), Mexico, Canada, China, Japan, South Korea, the United Kingdom, Vietnam, India, and Taiwan.[[347]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-366) The United States is the world's [largest importer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_imports "List of countries by imports") and [second-largest exporter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_exports "List of countries by exports").[[t]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-369) It is by far the world's [largest exporter of services](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_service_exports "List of countries by service exports").[[350]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-370)

Americans have the highest average [household](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Household_income "Household income")[[351]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-371) and [employee income](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_average_wage "List of countries by average wage") among OECD member states, and the fourth-highest [median household income](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Median_income "Median income") in 2023,[[352]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-372) up from sixth-highest in 2013.[[353]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Household_Income-373) With personal [consumption expenditures](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consumer_spending "Consumer spending") of over $18.5 trillion in 2023,[[354]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-374) the U.S. has a heavily [consumer-driven economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consumer_economy "Consumer economy") and is the world's [largest consumer market](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_largest_consumer_markets "List of largest consumer markets").[[355]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-375) The U.S. [ranked first in the number of dollar billionaires](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_billionaires "List of countries by number of billionaires") and [millionaires](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_millionaires "List of countries by number of millionaires") in 2023, with 735 billionaires and nearly 22 million millionaires.[[356]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-376)

[Wealth in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wealth_in_the_United_States "Wealth in the United States") is highly concentrated; in 2011, the richest 10% of the adult population owned 72% of the country's household wealth, while the bottom 50% owned just 2%.[[357]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-377)[U.S. wealth inequality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wealth_inequality_in_the_United_States "Wealth inequality in the United States") increased substantially since the late 1980s,[[358]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Smith-2022-378) and [income inequality in the U.S.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Income_inequality_in_the_United_States "Income inequality in the United States") reached a record high in 2019.[[359]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-379) In 2024, the country had some of the highest wealth and income inequality levels among [OECD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OECD "OECD") countries.[[360]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-380) Since the 1970s, there has been a decoupling of U.S. wage gains from worker productivity.[[361]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Hopkin-381) In 2016, the top fifth of earners took home more than half of all income,[[362]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-382) giving the U.S. one of the widest income distributions among OECD countries.[[363]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Sme-383)[[361]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Hopkin-381) There were about 771,480 [homeless persons in the U.S.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homelessness_in_the_United_States "Homelessness in the United States") in 2024.[[364]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-384) In 2022, 6.4 million children experienced food insecurity.[[365]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-ers.usda.gov-385)[Feeding America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feeding_America "Feeding America") estimates that around one in five, or approximately 13 million, [children experience hunger in the U.S.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hunger_in_the_United_States#Children "Hunger in the United States") and do not know where or when they will get their next meal.[[366]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FactsAbout-386) Also in 2022, about 37.9 million people, or 11.5% of the U.S. population, were [living in poverty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poverty_in_the_United_States "Poverty in the United States").[[367]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-387)

The United States has a smaller [welfare state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Welfare_state "Welfare state") and redistributes less income through government action than most other [high-income countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy "World Bank high-income economy").[[368]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-388)[[369]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-389) It is the only [advanced economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Advanced_economy "Advanced economy") that does not [guarantee its workers paid vacation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_statutory_minimum_employment_leave_by_country "List of statutory minimum employment leave by country") nationally[[370]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-390) and one of a few countries in the world without federal [paid family leave](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parental_leave_in_the_United_States "Parental leave in the United States") as a legal right.[[371]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-391) The United States has a higher percentage of low-income [workers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Working_class_in_the_United_States "Working class in the United States") than almost any other developed country, largely because of a weak [collective bargaining](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collective_bargaining "Collective bargaining") system and lack of government support for at-risk workers.[[372]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-392)

### Science and technology

Main articles: [Science and technology in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_the_United_States "Science and technology in the United States") and [Science policy of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science_policy_of_the_United_States "Science policy of the United States")

[![Image 54](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Aerial_view_of_Silicon_Valley.jpg/250px-Aerial_view_of_Silicon_Valley.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Aerial_view_of_Silicon_Valley.jpg)

California's [Silicon Valley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silicon_Valley "Silicon Valley") is the largest and foremost technology and innovation hub in the world.[[373]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-393)[[374]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-394)

The United States [has been a leader in technological innovation since the late 19th century](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technological_and_industrial_history_of_the_United_States "Technological and industrial history of the United States") and scientific research since the mid-20th century.[[375]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-395) Methods for producing [interchangeable parts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interchangeable_parts "Interchangeable parts") and the establishment of a [machine tool](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_tool "Machine tool") industry enabled [the large-scale manufacturing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_system_of_manufacturing "American system of manufacturing") of U.S. consumer products in the late 19th century.[[376]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-396) By the early 20th century, factory [electrification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrification "Electrification"), the introduction of the [assembly line](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assembly_line "Assembly line"), and other [labor-saving techniques](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automation "Automation") created the system of [mass production](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass_production "Mass production").[[377]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-397)

In the 21st century, the United States continues to be one of the world's foremost scientific powers,[[378]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-398) though China has emerged as a major competitor in many fields.[[379]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-399) The U.S. has the [highest research and development expenditures of any country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_by_research_and_development_spending "List of sovereign states by research and development spending")[[380]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-400) and ranks ninth as a percentage of GDP.[[381]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-401) In 2022, the United States was (after China) the country with the [second-highest number of published scientific papers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_scientific_and_technical_journal_articles "List of countries by number of scientific and technical journal articles").[[382]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-402) In 2021, the U.S. ranked second (also after China) by the number of patent applications, and third by trademark and industrial design applications (after China and Germany), according to [World Intellectual Property Indicators](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Intellectual_Property_Indicators "World Intellectual Property Indicators").[[383]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-403) In 2025[[384]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-404)[[385]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-405) the United States ranked third (after Switzerland and Sweden) in the [Global Innovation Index](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Innovation_Index "Global Innovation Index"). The United States is considered to be the leading country in the development of [artificial intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence "Artificial intelligence") technology.[[386]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-406) In 2023, the United States was ranked the second most technologically advanced country in the world (after South Korea) by _[Global Finance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global\_Finance\_(magazine) "Global Finance (magazine)")_ magazine.[[387]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-407)

#### Spaceflight

Main article: [Space policy of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_policy_of_the_United_States "Space policy of the United States")

[![Image 55](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/A_Man_on_the_Moon%2C_AS11-40-5903_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-A_Man_on_the_Moon%2C_AS11-40-5903_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:A_Man_on_the_Moon,_AS11-40-5903_(cropped).jpg)

Astronauts [Buzz Aldrin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buzz_Aldrin "Buzz Aldrin") and [Neil Armstrong](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neil_Armstrong "Neil Armstrong") (seen in visor reflection) during the 1969 [Apollo 11](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_11 "Apollo 11") mission, the first crewed [Moon landing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon_landing "Moon landing"). The United States is the only country to have landed humans on the Moon.

The United States has maintained a space program since the late 1950s, beginning with the establishment of the [National Aeronautics and Space Administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NASA "NASA") (NASA) in 1958.[[388]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-408)[[389]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-409) NASA's [Apollo program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_program "Apollo program") (1961â€“1972) achieved the first crewed [Moon landing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon_landing "Moon landing") with the 1969 [Apollo 11](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_11 "Apollo 11") mission; it remains one of the agency's most significant milestones.[[390]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-410)[[391]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-411) Other major endeavors by NASA include the [Space Shuttle program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_Shuttle_program "Space Shuttle program") (1981â€“2011),[[392]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-412) the [Voyager program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Voyager_program "Voyager program") (1972â€“present), the [Hubble](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope "Hubble Space Telescope") and [James Webb](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Webb_Space_Telescope "James Webb Space Telescope")[space telescopes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_telescope "Space telescope") (launched in 1990 and 2021, respectively),[[393]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-413)[[394]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-414) and the multi-mission [Mars Exploration Program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars_Exploration_Program "Mars Exploration Program") (_[Spirit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars\_Exploration\_Rover "Mars Exploration Rover")_ and _[Opportunity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opportunity\_(rover) "Opportunity (rover)")_, _[Curiosity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Curiosity\_(rover) "Curiosity (rover)"),_ and _[Perseverance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perseverance\_(rover) "Perseverance (rover)")_).[[395]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-415) NASA is one of five agencies collaborating on the [International Space Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Space_Station "International Space Station") (ISS);[[396]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-416) U.S. contributions to the ISS include several modules, including _[Destiny](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Destiny\_(ISS\_module) "Destiny (ISS module)")_ (2001), _[Harmony](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harmony\_(ISS\_module) "Harmony (ISS module)")_ (2007), and _[Tranquility](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tranquility\_(ISS\_module) "Tranquility (ISS module)")_ (2010), as well as ongoing logistical and operational support.[[397]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-417)

The United States [private sector](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Private_sector "Private sector") dominates the global [commercial spaceflight industry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Private_spaceflight "Private spaceflight").[[398]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-418) Prominent American spaceflight contractors include [Blue Origin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blue_Origin "Blue Origin"), [Boeing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boeing "Boeing"), [Lockheed Martin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lockheed_Martin "Lockheed Martin"), [Northrop Grumman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northrop_Grumman "Northrop Grumman"), and [SpaceX](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SpaceX "SpaceX"). NASA programs such as the [Commercial Crew Program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commercial_Crew_Program "Commercial Crew Program"), [Commercial Resupply Services](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commercial_Resupply_Services "Commercial Resupply Services"), [Commercial Lunar Payload Services](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commercial_Lunar_Payload_Services "Commercial Lunar Payload Services"), and [NextSTEP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Next_Space_Technologies_for_Exploration_Partnerships "Next Space Technologies for Exploration Partnerships") have facilitated growing private-sector involvement in American spaceflight.[[399]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-419)

### Energy

Main article: [Energy in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Energy_in_the_United_States "Energy in the United States")

In 2023, the United States received approximately 84% of its energy from fossil fuel, and its largest source of energy was [petroleum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petroleum_in_the_United_States "Petroleum in the United States") (38%), followed by [natural gas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_gas_in_the_United_States "Natural gas in the United States") (36%), [renewable sources](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Renewable_energy_in_the_United_States "Renewable energy in the United States") (9%), [coal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coal_in_the_United_States "Coal in the United States") (9%), and [nuclear power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_power_in_the_United_States "Nuclear power in the United States") (9%).[[400]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-420)[[401]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-visu-421) In 2022, the United States constituted about 4% of the [world's population](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_population "World population"), but [consumed around 16%](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_energy_consumption "List of countries by energy consumption") of the [world's energy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_energy_consumption "World energy consumption").[[402]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-422) The U.S. ranks as the [second-highest emitter of greenhouse gases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_greenhouse_gas_emissions "List of countries by greenhouse gas emissions") behind China.[[403]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-423)

The U.S. is the world's [largest producer of nuclear power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_power_by_country "Nuclear power by country"), generating around 30% of the world's nuclear electricity.[[404]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-424) It also has the highest number of nuclear power reactors of any country.[[405]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-425) From 2024, the U.S. plans to triple its nuclear power capacity by 2050.[[406]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-426)

### Transportation

Main article: [Transportation in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transportation_in_the_United_States "Transportation in the United States")

[![Image 56](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/45intoI-10_2.jpg/250px-45intoI-10_2.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:45intoI-10_2.jpg)

Interchange between [Interstate 10](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interstate_10 "Interstate 10") and [Interstate 45](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interstate_45 "Interstate 45") in [Houston](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houston "Houston"), Texas

The United States' 4 million miles (6.4 million kilometers) of road network, owned almost entirely by state and local governments, is the [longest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_road_network_size "List of countries by road network size") in the world.[[407]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-427)[[408]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-428) The extensive [Interstate Highway System](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interstate_Highway_System "Interstate Highway System") that connects all major U.S. cities is funded mostly by the federal government but maintained by [state departments of transportation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_and_insular_area_departments_of_transportation "List of U.S. state and insular area departments of transportation"). The system is further extended by [state highways](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_highway#United_States "State highway") and some private [toll roads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toll_road "Toll road").

The U.S. is among the top ten countries with the [highest vehicle ownership per capita](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_vehicles_per_capita "List of countries by vehicles per capita") (850 vehicles per 1,000 people) in 2022. A 2022 study found that 76% of U.S. commuters drive alone and 14% ride a bicycle, including bike owners and users of [bike-sharing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bike-sharing "Bike-sharing") networks. About 11% use some form of public transportation.[[409]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-429)[[410]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-430)

[Public transportation in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_transportation_in_the_United_States "Public transportation in the United States") is well developed in the largest urban areas, notably New York City, Washington, D.C., Boston, Philadelphia, Chicago, and San Francisco; otherwise, coverage is generally less extensive than in most other developed countries. The U.S. also has many relatively [car-dependent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Car-dependent "Car-dependent") localities.[[411]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-431)

Long-distance intercity travel is provided primarily by airlines, but travel by rail is more common along the [Northeast Corridor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northeast_Corridor "Northeast Corridor"), the only [high-speed rail in the U.S.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High-speed_rail_in_the_United_States "High-speed rail in the United States") that meets international standards. [Amtrak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amtrak "Amtrak"), the country's government-sponsored national passenger rail company, has a relatively sparse network compared to that of Western European countries. Service is concentrated in the Northeast, California, the Midwest, the Pacific Northwest, and Virginia/Southeast.

[![Image 57](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/ATL%281%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-ATL%281%29_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:ATL(1)_(cropped).jpg)

[Hartsfieldâ€“Jackson Atlanta International Airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hartsfield%E2%80%93Jackson_Atlanta_International_Airport "Hartsfieldâ€“Jackson Atlanta International Airport"), serving the [Atlanta metropolitan area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_metropolitan_area "Atlanta metropolitan area"), is the world's [busiest airport by passenger traffic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic "List of busiest airports by passenger traffic") with over 75 million passengers as of 2021.[[412]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-BusyAirport-432)[[413]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-433)

The United States has an extensive air transportation network. [U.S. civilian airlines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_airlines_of_the_United_States "List of airlines of the United States") are all privately owned. The three largest airlines in the world, by total number of passengers carried, are U.S.-based; [American Airlines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Airlines "American Airlines") became the global leader after its 2013 merger with [US Airways](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/US_Airways "US Airways").[[414]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-434) Of the 50 busiest airports in the world, 16 are in the United States, as well as five of the top 10.[[415]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-PANYNJ_2021_report-435) The world's busiest airport by passenger volume is [Hartsfieldâ€“Jackson Atlanta International](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hartsfield%E2%80%93Jackson_Atlanta_International_Airport "Hartsfieldâ€“Jackson Atlanta International Airport") in [Atlanta, Georgia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta "Atlanta").[[412]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-BusyAirport-432)[[415]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-PANYNJ_2021_report-435) In 2022, most of the [19,969 U.S. airports](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_airports_in_the_United_States "List of airports in the United States")[[416]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-436) were owned and operated by local government authorities, and there are also some private airports. Some 5,193 are designated as "public use", including for [general aviation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_aviation "General aviation"). The [Transportation Security Administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transportation_Security_Administration "Transportation Security Administration") (TSA) has provided security at most major airports since 2001.

[The country's rail transport network](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rail_transport_in_the_United_States "Rail transport in the United States"), the [longest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_rail_transport_network_size "List of countries by rail transport network size") in the world at 182,412.3 mi (293,564.2 km),[[417]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-437) handles mostly [freight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freight_transport "Freight transport")[[418]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-438)[[419]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-439) (in contrast to more passenger-centered rail in Europe[[420]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-440)). Because they are often privately owned operations, U.S. railroads lag behind those of the rest of the world in terms of electrification.[[421]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-441)

[The country's inland waterways](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inland_waterways_of_the_United_States "Inland waterways of the United States") are the world's [fifth-longest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_waterways_length "List of countries by waterways length"), totaling 25,482 mi (41,009 km).[[422]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-442) They are used extensively for freight, recreation, and a small amount of passenger traffic. Of the world's [50 busiest container ports](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_busiest_container_ports "List of busiest container ports"), four are located in the United States, with the busiest in the country being the [Port of Los Angeles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Port_of_Los_Angeles "Port of Los Angeles").[[423]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-443)

Demographics
------------

Main article: [Demographics of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demographics_of_the_United_States "Demographics of the United States")

### Population

Main articles: [Americans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Americans "Americans") and [Race and ethnicity in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Race_and_ethnicity_in_the_United_States "Race and ethnicity in the United States")

See also: [List of U.S. states by population](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_population "List of U.S. states by population")

The 10 most populous U.S. states 

 (2024 estimates)[[424]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-CensusEst2024-444)| State | Population (millions) |
| --- | --- |
| [California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California "California") | 39.4 |
| [Texas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texas "Texas") | 31.3 |
| [Florida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Florida "Florida") | 23.4 |
| [New York](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_(state) "New York (state)") | 19.9 |
| [Pennsylvania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pennsylvania "Pennsylvania") | 13.1 |
| [Illinois](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Illinois "Illinois") | 12.7 |
| [Ohio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ohio "Ohio") | 11.9 |
| [Georgia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state) "Georgia (U.S. state)") | 11.2 |
| [North Carolina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Carolina "North Carolina") | 11.0 |
| [Michigan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michigan "Michigan") | 10.1 |

The [U.S. Census Bureau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau "United States Census Bureau") reported 331,449,281 residents on April 1, 2020,[[u]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-445)[[425]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-2020CENSUS-446) making the United States the [third-most-populous country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population "List of countries and dependencies by population") in the world, after China and India.[[345]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-CIA-2018-364) The Census Bureau's official 2024 population estimate was 340,110,988, an increase of 2.6% since the 2020 census.[[13]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Vintage2024-16) According to the Bureau's [U.S. Population Clock](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._and_World_Population_Clock "U.S. and World Population Clock"), on July 1, 2024, the U.S. population had a net gain of one person every 16 seconds, or about 5400 people per day.[[426]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-447) In 2023, 51% of Americans age 15 and over were married, 6% were [widowed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Widowed "Widowed"), 10% were divorced, and 34% had never been married.[[427]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-448) In 2023, the [total fertility rate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Total_fertility_rate "Total fertility rate") for the U.S. stood at 1.6 children per woman,[[428]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-449) and, at 23%, it had the world's highest rate of children living in [single-parent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Single_parents_in_the_United_States "Single parents in the United States") households in 2019.[[429]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-450)

The United States has a diverse population; 37 [ancestry groups](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_ancestries "American ancestries") have more than one million members.[[430]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-An2000-451)[White Americans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-Hispanic_whites "Non-Hispanic whites") with ancestry from Europe, the Middle East, or North Africa form the largest [racial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Race_(human_classification) "Race (human classification)") and [ethnic group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_group "Ethnic group") at 57.8% of the United States population.[[431]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-452)[[432]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-453)[Hispanic and Latino Americans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans "Hispanic and Latino Americans") form the second-largest group and are 18.7% of the United States population. [African Americans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/African_Americans "African Americans") constitute the country's third-largest ancestry group and are 12.1% of the total U.S. population.[[430]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-An2000-451) Asian Americans are the country's fourth-largest group, composing 5.9% of the United States population. The country's 3.7 million Native Americans account for about 1%,[[430]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-An2000-451) and some 574 native tribes are recognized by the federal government.[[433]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-454) In 2024, the [median age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Median_age "Median age") of the United States population was 39.1 years.[[434]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-455)

### Language

Main article: [Languages of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Languages_of_the_United_States "Languages of the United States")

[![Image 58](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Languages_cp-02.svg/250px-Languages_cp-02.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Languages_cp-02.svg)

Most spoken languages in the U.S.

While many languages are spoken in the United States, [English](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_English "American English") is by far the most commonly spoken and written.[[435]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-456)_[De facto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De\_facto "De facto")_, English is the [official language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Official_language "Official language") of the United States, and in 2025, [Executive Order 14224](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_Order_14224 "Executive Order 14224") declared English official.[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-EOWP-4) However, the U.S. has never had a _[de jure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De\_jure "De jure")_ official language, as Congress has never passed a law to designate English as official for all three federal branches. Some laws, such as [U.S. naturalization requirements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naturalized_citizen_of_the_United_States "Naturalized citizen of the United States"), nonetheless standardize English. Twenty-eight states and the [United States Virgin Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands "United States Virgin Islands") have laws that designate English as the sole official language; 19 states and the [District of Columbia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/District_of_Columbia "District of Columbia") have no official language.[[436]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-457) Three states and four U.S. territories have recognized local or indigenous languages in addition to English: Hawaii ([Hawaiian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hawaiian_language "Hawaiian language")),[[437]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-458) Alaska ([twenty Native languages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alaska_Native_languages "Alaska Native languages")),[[v]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-459)[[438]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-460) South Dakota ([Sioux](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sioux_language "Sioux language")),[[439]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-LakotaCommon-461) American Samoa ([Samoan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samoan_language "Samoan language")), Puerto Rico ([Spanish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_language_in_the_United_States "Spanish language in the United States")), Guam ([Chamorro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chamorro_language "Chamorro language")), and the Northern Mariana Islands ([Carolinian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carolinian_language "Carolinian language") and Chamorro). In total, 169 Native American languages are spoken in the United States.[[440]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-462) In Puerto Rico, Spanish is more widely spoken than English.[[441]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-PuertoRicoTranslation-463)

According to the [American Community Survey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Community_Survey "American Community Survey") (2020),[[442]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-ACS2021-464) some 245.4 million people in the U.S. age five and older spoke only English at home. About 41.2 million spoke Spanish at home, making it the second most commonly used language. Other languages spoken at home by one million people or more include [Chinese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_language_in_the_United_States "Chinese language in the United States") (3.40 million), [Tagalog](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tagalog_language_in_the_United_States "Tagalog language in the United States") (1.71 million), [Vietnamese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vietnamese_language_in_the_United_States "Vietnamese language in the United States") (1.52 million), [Arabic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic_language_in_the_United_States "Arabic language in the United States") (1.39 million), [French](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_language_in_the_United_States "French language in the United States") (1.18 million), [Korean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Korean_language_in_the_United_States "Korean language in the United States") (1.07 million), and [Russian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_language_in_the_United_States "Russian language in the United States") (1.04 million). [German](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language_in_the_United_States "German language in the United States"), spoken by 1 million people at home in 2010, fell to 857,000 total speakers in 2020.[[443]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-465)

### Immigration

Main article: [Immigration to the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immigration_to_the_United_States "Immigration to the United States")

[![Image 59](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Border_USA_Mexico.jpg/250px-Border_USA_Mexico.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Border_USA_Mexico.jpg)

The [Mexicoâ€“United States border wall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexico%E2%80%93United_States_border_wall "Mexicoâ€“United States border wall") between [San Diego](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Diego "San Diego") (left) and [Tijuana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tijuana "Tijuana") (right)

America's immigrant population is by far the world's [largest in absolute terms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_by_immigrant_population "List of sovereign states and dependent territories by immigrant population").[[444]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-UNdef-466)[[445]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-467) In 2022, there were 87.7 million immigrants and [U.S.-born children of immigrants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second-generation_immigrants_in_the_United_States "Second-generation immigrants in the United States") in the United States, accounting for nearly 27% of the overall U.S. population.[[446]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-468) In 2017, out of the U.S. foreign-born population, some 45% (20.7 million) were naturalized citizens, 27% (12.3 million) were lawful permanent residents, 6% (2.2 million) were temporary lawful residents, and 23% (10.5 million) were [unauthorized immigrants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Undocumented_immigrant_population_of_the_United_States "Undocumented immigrant population of the United States").[[447]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-KeyFindings-469) In 2019, the top countries of origin for immigrants were Mexico (24% of immigrants), India (6%), China (5%), the Philippines (4.5%), and El Salvador (3%).[[448]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-470) In fiscal year 2022, over one million immigrants (most of whom entered through [family reunification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chain_migration#Legislation "Chain migration")) were granted [legal residence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permanent_residence_(United_States) "Permanent residence (United States)").[[449]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-471) The undocumented immigrant population in the U.S. reached a record high of 14 million in 2023.[[450]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-472)

### Religion

Main article: [Religion in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion_in_the_United_States "Religion in the United States")

Religious affiliation in the U.S., according to a 2023 [Gallup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gallup,_Inc. "Gallup, Inc.") poll:[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Staff-2007-10)

1.   [Protestantism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protestantism_in_the_United_States "Protestantism in the United States") (33.0%)
2.   [Catholicism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_the_United_States "Catholic Church in the United States") (22.0%)
3.   [Non-specific Christian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianity_in_the_United_States "Christianity in the United States") (11.0%)
4.   [Judaism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judaism_in_the_United_States "Judaism in the United States") (2.00%)
5.   [Mormonism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mormonism_in_the_United_States "Mormonism in the United States") (1.00%)
6.   Other religion (6.00%)
7.   [Unaffiliated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irreligion_in_the_United_States "Irreligion in the United States") (22.0%)
8.   Unanswered (3.00%)

The [First Amendment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution "First Amendment to the United States Constitution") guarantees the [free exercise of religion in the country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_Exercise_Clause "Free Exercise Clause") and forbids Congress from passing laws respecting [its establishment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Establishment_Clause "Establishment Clause").[[451]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Donadio-2021-473)[[452]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-474) Religious practice is widespread, among the [most diverse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_ethnic_and_cultural_diversity_level "List of countries by ethnic and cultural diversity level") in the world,[[453]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-alesina1-475) and profoundly vibrant.

[[454]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-pewreligion-476) The country has the world's [largest Christian population](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianity_by_country "Christianity by country"), which includes the [fourth-largest population of Catholics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catholic_Church_by_country "Catholic Church by country").[[455]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Global_Christianity-477) Other notable faiths include [Judaism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judaism "Judaism"), [Buddhism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddhism "Buddhism"), [Hinduism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hinduism "Hinduism"), [Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam "Islam"), [New Age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Age "New Age"), and [Native American religions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Native_American_religions "Native American religions").[[456]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-478) Religious practice varies significantly by region.[[457]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Williams-2023-479) "[Ceremonial deism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ceremonial_deism "Ceremonial deism")" is common in American culture.[[458]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-480)

The overwhelming majority of [Americans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Americans "Americans") believe in a [higher power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Higher_Power "Higher Power") or spiritual force, engage in [spiritual practices](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spiritual_practice "Spiritual practice") such as prayer, and consider themselves religious or [spiritual](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spirituality "Spirituality").[[459]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Kallo-2023-481)[[460]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-482) In the Southern United States' "[Bible Belt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bible_Belt "Bible Belt")", [evangelical Protestantism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evangelicalism "Evangelicalism") plays a significant role culturally; [New England](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_England "New England") and the Western United States [tend to be more secular](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unchurched_Belt "Unchurched Belt").[[457]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Williams-2023-479)[[461]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-483)[Mormonism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mormonism "Mormonism"), a [Restorationist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Restorationism "Restorationism") movement founded in the U.S. in 1847,[[462]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHowe2008727%E2%80%93728-484) is the predominant religion in Utah and a major religion in Idaho.

### Urbanization

Main articles: [Urbanization in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urbanization_in_the_United_States "Urbanization in the United States") and [List of United States cities by population](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population "List of United States cities by population")

About 82% of Americans live in [urban areas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_urban_area "United States urban area"), including suburbs;[[345]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-CIA-2018-364) about half of those reside in cities with populations over 50,000.[[463]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-485) In 2022, 333 [incorporated municipalities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population "List of United States cities by population") had populations over 100,000, nine cities had more than one million residents, and four citiesâ€”[New York City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_City "New York City"), [Los Angeles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles "Los Angeles"), [Chicago](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chicago "Chicago"), and [Houston](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houston "Houston")â€”had populations exceeding two million.[[464]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-486) Many U.S. metropolitan populations are growing rapidly, particularly in the South and West.[[465]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-487)

| 10 | [Phoenix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phoenix_metropolitan_area "Phoenix metropolitan area") | [West](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_United_States "Western United States") | 5,186,958 | 20 | [Orlando](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greater_Orlando "Greater Orlando") | [South](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_United_States "Southern United States") | 2,940,513 |

### Health

Main article: [Health in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Health_in_the_United_States "Health in the United States")

Further information: [Healthcare in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Healthcare_in_the_United_States "Healthcare in the United States") and [Health insurance in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Health_insurance_in_the_United_States "Health insurance in the United States")

[![Image 60](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Texas_medical_center.jpg/250px-Texas_medical_center.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Texas_medical_center.jpg)

The [Texas Medical Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texas_Medical_Center "Texas Medical Center") in [Houston](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houston "Houston") is the largest medical complex in the world.[[467]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-489)[[468]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-490) In 2018, it employed 120,000 people and treated 10 million patients.[[469]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-491)

According to the [Centers for Disease Control and Prevention](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention "Centers for Disease Control and Prevention") (CDC), average American life expectancy at birth was 78.4 years in 2023 (75.8 years for men and 81.1 years for women). This was a gain of 0.9 year from 77.5 years in 2022, and the CDC noted that the new average was largely driven by "decreases in mortality due to COVID-19, heart disease, unintentional injuries, cancer and diabetes".[[470]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-492) Starting in 1998, life expectancy in the U.S. fell [behind that of other wealthy industrialized countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_life_expectancy "List of countries by life expectancy"), and Americans' "health disadvantage" gap has been increasing ever since.[[471]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-493)

The Commonwealth Fund reported in 2020 that the U.S. had the [highest suicide rate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_suicide_rate "List of countries by suicide rate") among [high-income countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High-income_countries "High-income countries").[[472]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-494)[Approximately one-third of the U.S. adult population is obese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Obesity_in_the_United_States "Obesity in the United States") and another third is overweight.[[473]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-495) The U.S. healthcare system far [outspends that of any other country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_total_health_expenditure_(PPP)_per_capita "List of countries by total health expenditure (PPP) per capita"), measured both in per capita spending and as a percentage of GDP, but attains worse healthcare outcomes when compared to peer countries for reasons that are debated.[[474]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-496) The United States is the only developed country [without a system of universal healthcare](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Healthcare_reform_in_the_United_States "Healthcare reform in the United States"), and [a significant proportion of the population that does not carry health insurance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Health_insurance_coverage_in_the_United_States "Health insurance coverage in the United States").[[475]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-497) Government-funded healthcare coverage for the poor ([Medicaid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medicaid "Medicaid")) and for those age 65 and older ([Medicare](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medicare_(United_States) "Medicare (United States)")) is available to Americans who meet the programs' income or age qualifications. In 2010, then-President Obama passed the [Patient Protection and Affordable Care Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patient_Protection_and_Affordable_Care_Act "Patient Protection and Affordable Care Act").[[w]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-498)[[476]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-499)[Abortion in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abortion_in_the_United_States "Abortion in the United States") is not federally protected, and is illegal or restricted in 17 states.[[477]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-500)

### Education

Main article: [Education in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Education_in_the_United_States "Education in the United States")

[![Image 61: Photograph of the University of Virginia](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/University_of_Virginia_Rotunda_in_2006.jpg/250px-University_of_Virginia_Rotunda_in_2006.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:University_of_Virginia_Rotunda_in_2006.jpg)

Some 77% of American college students attend public institutions[[478]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-501) such as the [University of Virginia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Virginia "University of Virginia"), founded by [Thomas Jefferson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson "Thomas Jefferson") in 1819.

American primary and secondary education, known in the U.S. as [Kâ€“12](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/K%E2%80%9312_education_in_the_United_States "Kâ€“12 education in the United States") ("kindergarten through 12th grade"), is decentralized. School systems are operated by state, territorial, and sometimes municipal governments and regulated by the [U.S. Department of Education](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Education "United States Department of Education"). In general, children are required to attend school or [an approved homeschool](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homeschooling_in_the_United_States "Homeschooling in the United States") from the age of five or six ([kindergarten](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kindergarten "Kindergarten") or [first grade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_grade "First grade")) until they are 18 years old. This often brings students through the [12th grade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twelfth_grade "Twelfth grade"), the final year of a U.S. high school, but some states and territories allow them to leave school earlier, at age 16 or 17.[[479]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-502) The U.S. spends more on education per student than any other country,[[480]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-503) an average of $18,614 per year per public elementary and secondary school student in 2020â€“2021.[[481]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-504) Among Americans age 25 and older, 92.2% graduated from high school, 62.7% attended some college, 37.7% earned a [bachelor's degree](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree "Bachelor's degree"), and 14.2% earned a graduate degree.[[482]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-505) The [U.S. literacy rate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literacy_in_the_United_States "Literacy in the United States") is near-universal.[[345]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-CIA-2018-364)[[483]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-506) The U.S. has produced the [most Nobel Prize winners of any country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_by_country "List of Nobel laureates by country"), with [411](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_American_Nobel_laureates "List of American Nobel laureates") (having won 413 awards).[[484]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-507)[[485]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-508)

[U.S. tertiary or higher education](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Higher_education_in_the_United_States "Higher education in the United States") has earned a global reputation. Many of the world's top universities, as listed by various ranking organizations, are in the United States, including 19 of the top 25.[[486]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-509)[[487]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-510) American higher education is dominated by [state university systems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_university_system "State university system"), although [the country's many private universities and colleges](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Private_universities_in_the_United_States "Private universities in the United States") enroll about 20% of all American students. Local [community colleges](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Community_colleges_in_the_United_States "Community colleges in the United States") generally offer [open admissions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open_admissions "Open admissions"), lower tuition, and coursework leading to a two-year [associate degree](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Associate_degree "Associate degree") or a [non-degree certificate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Certificate_program "Certificate program").[[488]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-511)

As for [public expenditures](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_expenditure "Public expenditure") on higher education, the U.S. spends more per student than the [OECD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OECD "OECD") average, and Americans spend more than all nations in combined public and private spending.[[489]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-education_spending-512) Colleges and universities directly funded by the federal government do not charge tuition and are limited to military personnel and government employees, including: the [U.S. service academies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_service_academies "United States service academies"), the [Naval Postgraduate School](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naval_Postgraduate_School "Naval Postgraduate School"), and [military staff colleges](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/US_military_staff_colleges "US military staff colleges"). Despite some student [loan forgiveness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Loan_forgiveness "Loan forgiveness") programs in place,[[490]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-513)[student loan debt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Student_debt "Student debt") increased by 102% between 2010 and 2020,[[491]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-514) and exceeded $1.7 trillion in 2022.[[492]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-515)

Culture and society
-------------------

Main articles: [Culture of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_States "Culture of the United States") and [Society of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Society_of_the_United_States "Society of the United States")

See also: [Human rights in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_rights_in_the_United_States "Human rights in the United States")

[![Image 62: The Statue of Liberty, a large teal bronze sculpture on a stone pedestal](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Statue_of_Liberty_frontal_2_crop.JPG/250px-Statue_of_Liberty_frontal_2_crop.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Statue_of_Liberty_frontal_2_crop.JPG)

The [Statue of Liberty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statue_of_Liberty "Statue of Liberty") (_Liberty Enlightening the World_) on [Liberty Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberty_Island "Liberty Island") in [New York Harbor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Harbor "New York Harbor") was an 1866 gift from France that has become an iconic symbol of the [American Dream](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Dream "American Dream").[[493]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-516)

The United States is home to [a wide variety of ethnic groups, traditions, and customs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multiculturalism_in_the_United_States "Multiculturalism in the United States").[[494]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-517)[[495]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-518) The country has been described as having [the values](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Americanism_(ideology) "Americanism (ideology)") of [individualism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Individualism "Individualism") and [personal autonomy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Left-libertarianism "Left-libertarianism"),[[496]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-519)[[497]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-520) as well as a strong [work ethic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Work_ethic "Work ethic")[[498]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-521) and [competitiveness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Competition "Competition").[[499]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-522) Voluntary [altruism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Altruism "Altruism") towards others also plays a major role;[[500]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-523)[[501]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-524)[[502]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-525) according to a 2016 study by the [Charities Aid Foundation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charities_Aid_Foundation "Charities Aid Foundation"), Americans donated 1.44% of total GDP to charityâ€”the [highest rate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_charitable_donation "List of countries by charitable donation") in the world by a large margin.[[503]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-526) Americans have traditionally [been characterized](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stereotypes_of_Americans "Stereotypes of Americans") by a unifying political belief in an "[American Creed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Creed "American Creed")" emphasizing [consent of the governed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consent_of_the_governed "Consent of the governed"), [liberty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberty "Liberty"), [equality under the law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equality_under_the_law "Equality under the law"), [democracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democracy "Democracy"), [social equality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_equality "Social equality"), [property rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Property_rights "Property rights"), and a preference for [limited government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Limited_government "Limited government").[[504]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-527)[[505]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-528) The U.S. has acquired significant [hard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hard_power "Hard power") and [soft power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soft_power "Soft power") through [its diplomatic influence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_United_States "Foreign relations of the United States"), [economic power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_power "Economic power"), [military alliances](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_alliance "Military alliance"), and [cultural exports](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultural_exports "Cultural exports") such as [American movies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cinema_of_the_United_States "Cinema of the United States"), [music](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Music_of_the_United_States "Music of the United States"), [video games](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Video_games_in_the_United_States "Video games in the United States"), [sports](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sports_in_the_United_States "Sports in the United States"), and [food](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_cuisine "American cuisine").[[506]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-529)[[507]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-530) The influence that the United States exerts on other countries through soft power is referred to as [Americanization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Americanization "Americanization").[[508]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-531)

Nearly all present Americans or their ancestors came from [Europe, Africa, or Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afro-Eurasia "Afro-Eurasia") (the "[Old World](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_World "Old World")") within the past five centuries.[[509]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-532)[Mainstream](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/mainstream "wikt:mainstream") American culture is a [Western culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_culture "Western culture") largely derived from the [traditions of European immigrants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_American#Culture "European American") with influences from many other sources, such as [traditions brought by slaves from Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/African-American_culture "African-American culture").[[510]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-533) More recent immigration from [Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asian_American "Asian American") and especially [Latin America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin_American_culture "Latin American culture") has added to a cultural mix that has been described as a homogenizing [melting pot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Melting_pot "Melting pot"), and a heterogeneous [salad bowl](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salad_bowl_(cultural_idea) "Salad bowl (cultural idea)"), with immigrants contributing to, and often [assimilating](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assimilation_(phonology) "Assimilation (phonology)") into, mainstream American culture.

Under the [First Amendment to the Constitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution "First Amendment to the United States Constitution"), the United States is considered to have the [strongest protections of free speech of any country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_speech_in_the_United_States "Freedom of speech in the United States").[[511]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Coleman-2013-534)[Flag desecration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flag_desecration_in_the_United_States "Flag desecration in the United States"), [hate speech](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hate_speech_in_the_United_States "Hate speech in the United States"), [blasphemy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blasphemy_law_in_the_United_States "Blasphemy law in the United States"), and [lese majesty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/L%C3%A8se-majest%C3%A9 "LÃ¨se-majestÃ©") are all forms of protected expression.[[512]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-535)[[513]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-536)[[514]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-537) A 2016 [Pew Research Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pew_Research_Center "Pew Research Center") poll found that Americans were the most supportive of free expression of any polity measured.[[515]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-538) Additionally, they are the "most supportive of [freedom of the press](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_the_press_in_the_United_States "Freedom of the press in the United States") and the [right to use the Internet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Right_to_Internet_access "Right to Internet access") without government censorship".[[516]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-539) The U.S. is a [socially progressive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultural_liberalism "Cultural liberalism") country[[517]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-540) with [permissive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permissive_society "Permissive society") attitudes surrounding [human sexuality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_sexuality "Human sexuality").[[518]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Derks-2020-541)[LGBTQ rights in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LGBTQ_rights_in_the_United_States "LGBTQ rights in the United States") are among the most advanced by global standards.[[518]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Derks-2020-541)[[519]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-542)[[520]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-543)

The [American Dream](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Dream "American Dream"), or the perception that Americans enjoy high levels of [social mobility](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socio-economic_mobility_in_the_United_States "Socio-economic mobility in the United States"), plays a key role in attracting immigrants.[[521]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-544)[[522]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-545) Whether this perception is accurate has been a topic of debate.[[523]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-socialmobility-546)[[524]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-CAP-547)[[525]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-548) While mainstream culture holds that the United States is a [classless society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Classless_society "Classless society"),[[526]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-549) scholars identify significant differences between [the country's social classes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_class_in_the_United_States "Social class in the United States"), affecting [socialization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialization "Socialization"), language, and values.[[527]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-550)[[528]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-551) Americans tend to greatly value [socioeconomic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socioeconomics "Socioeconomics") achievement, but [being ordinary or average](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Average_Joe "Average Joe") is promoted by some as a noble condition as well.[[529]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-552)

The [National Foundation on the Arts and the Humanities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Foundation_on_the_Arts_and_the_Humanities "National Foundation on the Arts and the Humanities") is an agency of the United States federal government that was established in 1965 with the purpose to "develop and promote a broadly conceived national policy of support for the humanities and the arts in the United States, and for institutions which preserve the cultural heritage of the United States."[[530]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-553) It is composed of four sub-agencies:

*   [National Endowment for the Arts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Endowment_for_the_Arts "National Endowment for the Arts")
*   [National Endowment for the Humanities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Endowment_for_the_Humanities "National Endowment for the Humanities")
*   [Institute of Museum and Library Services](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institute_of_Museum_and_Library_Services "Institute of Museum and Library Services")
*   [Federal Council on the Arts and the Humanities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Council_on_the_Arts_and_the_Humanities "Federal Council on the Arts and the Humanities")

### Literature

Main article: [American literature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_literature "American literature")

See also: [American philosophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_philosophy "American philosophy")

[![Image 63: Photograph of Mark Twain](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Mark_Twain_by_AF_Bradley.jpg/250px-Mark_Twain_by_AF_Bradley.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Mark_Twain_by_AF_Bradley.jpg)

[Mark Twain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_Twain "Mark Twain"), whom [William Faulkner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Faulkner "William Faulkner") called "the father of American literature"[[531]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-faulkner-554)

Colonial American authors were influenced by [John Locke](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Locke "John Locke") and other [Enlightenment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment "Age of Enlightenment") philosophers.[[532]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaymLevine2013157%E2%80%93159-555)[[533]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTELauter1994a503%E2%80%93509-556) The [American Revolutionary Period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Revolution "American Revolution") (1765â€“1783) is notable for the political writings of [Benjamin Franklin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benjamin_Franklin "Benjamin Franklin"), [Alexander Hamilton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_Hamilton "Alexander Hamilton"), [Thomas Paine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Paine "Thomas Paine"), and [Thomas Jefferson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson "Thomas Jefferson"). Shortly before and after the [Revolutionary War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War "American Revolutionary War"), the newspaper rose to prominence, filling a demand for anti-British national literature.[[534]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaymLevine2013163-557)[[535]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-558) An early novel is [William Hill Brown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Hill_Brown "William Hill Brown")'s _[The Power of Sympathy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Power\_of\_Sympathy "The Power of Sympathy")_, published in 1791. Writer and critic [John Neal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Neal "John Neal") in the early- to mid-19th century helped advance America toward a unique literature and culture by criticizing predecessors such as [Washington Irving](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington_Irving "Washington Irving") for imitating their British counterparts, and by influencing writers such as [Edgar Allan Poe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edgar_Allan_Poe "Edgar Allan Poe"),[[536]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-559) who took American poetry and short fiction in new directions. [Ralph Waldo Emerson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ralph_Waldo_Emerson "Ralph Waldo Emerson") and [Margaret Fuller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Margaret_Fuller "Margaret Fuller") pioneered the influential [Transcendentalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transcendentalism "Transcendentalism") movement;[[537]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-560)[[538]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Coviello-561)[Henry David Thoreau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_David_Thoreau "Henry David Thoreau"), author of _[Walden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walden "Walden")_, was influenced by this movement.

The conflict surrounding [abolitionism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_States "Abolitionism in the United States") inspired writers, like [Harriet Beecher Stowe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harriet_Beecher_Stowe "Harriet Beecher Stowe"), and authors of slave narratives, such as [Frederick Douglass](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frederick_Douglass "Frederick Douglass"). [Nathaniel Hawthorne](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nathaniel_Hawthorne "Nathaniel Hawthorne")'s _[The Scarlet Letter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Scarlet\_Letter "The Scarlet Letter")_ (1850) explored the dark side of American history, as did [Herman Melville](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herman_Melville "Herman Melville")'s _[Moby-Dick](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moby-Dick "Moby-Dick")_ (1851).
