Major American poets of the 19th century [American Renaissance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Renaissance_(literature) "American Renaissance (literature)") include [Walt Whitman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walt_Whitman "Walt Whitman"), Melville, and [Emily Dickinson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emily_Dickinson "Emily Dickinson").[[539]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaymLevine2013444%E2%80%93447-562)[[540]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTELauter1994a1228,_1233,_1260-563)[Mark Twain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_Twain "Mark Twain") was the first major American writer to be born in the West. [Henry James](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_James "Henry James") achieved international recognition with novels like _[The Portrait of a Lady](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Portrait\_of\_a\_Lady "The Portrait of a Lady")_ (1881). As literacy rates rose, periodicals published more stories centered around industrial workers, women, and the rural poor.[[541]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaymLevine20131269%E2%80%931270-564)[[542]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTELauter1994b8%E2%80%9310-565)[Naturalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naturalism_(literature) "Naturalism (literature)"), [regionalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_literary_regionalism "American literary regionalism"), and [realism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literary_realism#UnitedStates "Literary realism") were the major literary movements of the period.[[543]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaymLevine20131271%E2%80%931273-566)[[544]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTELauter1994b12-567)

While [modernism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literary_modernism "Literary modernism") generally took on an international character, modernist authors working within the United States more often rooted their work in specific regions, peoples, and cultures.[[545]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaymLevine20131850%E2%80%931851-568) Following the Great Migration to northern cities, African-American and black [West Indian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Indian_Americans "West Indian Americans") authors of the [Harlem Renaissance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harlem_Renaissance "Harlem Renaissance") developed an independent tradition of literature that rebuked a history of inequality and celebrated black culture. An important cultural export during the [Jazz Age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jazz_Age "Jazz Age"), these writings were a key influence on _[NÃ©gritude](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/N%C3%A9gritude "NÃ©gritude")_, a philosophy emerging in the 1930s among francophone writers of the [African diaspora](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/African_diaspora "African diaspora").[[546]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-569)[[547]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-570) In the 1950s, an ideal of homogeneity led many authors to attempt to write the [Great American Novel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_American_Novel "Great American Novel"),[[548]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaymLevine20132260%E2%80%932261-571) while the [Beat Generation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beat_Generation "Beat Generation") rejected this conformity, using styles that elevated the impact of the [spoken word](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spoken_word "Spoken word") over mechanics to describe drug use, sexuality, and the failings of society.[[549]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaymLevine20132262-572)[[550]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-573) Contemporary literature is more pluralistic than in previous eras, with the closest thing to a unifying feature being a trend toward self-conscious [experiments with language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Experimental_literature "Experimental literature").[[551]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaymLevine20132266%E2%80%932267-574) Twelve American laureates have won the [Nobel Prize in Literature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature "Nobel Prize in Literature").[[552]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-575)

### Mass media

Main article: [Mass media in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass_media_in_the_United_States "Mass media in the United States")

See also: [Newspapers in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newspapers_in_the_United_States "Newspapers in the United States"), [Television in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Television_in_the_United_States "Television in the United States"), [Broadcasting in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Broadcasting_in_the_United_States "Broadcasting in the United States"), [Public broadcasting in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_broadcasting_in_the_United_States "Public broadcasting in the United States"), [Internet in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet_in_the_United_States "Internet in the United States"), [Radio in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radio_in_the_United_States "Radio in the United States"), and [Video games in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Video_games_in_the_United_States "Video games in the United States")

[![Image 64](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Comcast_Center_2018.jpg/250px-Comcast_Center_2018.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Comcast_Center_2018.jpg)

[Comcast Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comcast_Center "Comcast Center") in [Philadelphia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philadelphia "Philadelphia"), headquarters of [Comcast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comcast "Comcast"), one of the world's [largest telecommunications companies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_telecommunications_companies "List of telecommunications companies") and media conglomerates

Media in the United States is [broadly uncensored](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Censorship_in_the_United_States "Censorship in the United States"), with the [First Amendment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution "First Amendment to the United States Constitution") providing significant protections, as reiterated in _[New York Times Co. v. United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New\_York\_Times\_Co.\_v.\_United\_States "New York Times Co. v. United States")_.[[511]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Coleman-2013-534) The four major broadcasters in the U.S. are the [National Broadcasting Company](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Broadcasting_Company "National Broadcasting Company") (NBC), [Columbia Broadcasting System](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Columbia_Broadcasting_System "Columbia Broadcasting System") (CBS), [American Broadcasting Company](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company "American Broadcasting Company") (ABC), and [Fox Broadcasting Company](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company "Fox Broadcasting Company") (FOX). The four major broadcast television networks are all commercial entities. The [U.S. cable television system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cable_television_in_the_United_States "Cable television in the United States") offers hundreds of channels catering to a variety of niches.[[553]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-576) In 2021, about 83% of Americans over age 12 listened to [broadcast radio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radio_broadcasting "Radio broadcasting"), while about 40% listened to [podcasts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Podcast "Podcast").[[554]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-577) In the prior year, there were 15,460 licensed full-power radio stations in the U.S. according to the [Federal Communications Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Communications_Commission "Federal Communications Commission") (FCC).[[555]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-578) Much of the public radio broadcasting is supplied by [NPR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NPR "NPR"), incorporated in February 1970 under the [Public Broadcasting Act of 1967](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_Broadcasting_Act_of_1967 "Public Broadcasting Act of 1967").[[556]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-579)

U.S. newspapers with a global reach and reputation include _[The Wall Street Journal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Wall\_Street\_Journal "The Wall Street Journal")_, _[The New York Times](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_New\_York\_Times "The New York Times")_, _[The Washington Post](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Washington\_Post "The Washington Post")_, and _[USA Today](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/USA\_Today "USA Today")_.[[557]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Shaffer2006-580)[About 800 publications](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Spanish-language_newspapers_published_in_the_United_States "List of Spanish-language newspapers published in the United States") are produced in Spanish.[[558]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-581)[[559]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-582) With few exceptions, newspapers are privately owned, either by large chains such as [Gannett](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gannett_Company "Gannett Company") or [McClatchy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_McClatchy_Company "The McClatchy Company"), which own dozens or even hundreds of newspapers; by small chains that own a handful of papers; or, in an increasingly rare situation, by individuals or families. Major cities often have [alternative newspapers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alternative_newspaper "Alternative newspaper") to complement the mainstream daily papers, such as _[The Village Voice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Village\_Voice "The Village Voice")_ in New York City and _[LA Weekly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LA\_Weekly "LA Weekly")_ in Los Angeles. The five most popular websites used in the U.S. are [Google](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Google_Search "Google Search"), [YouTube](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/YouTube "YouTube"), [Facebook](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Facebook "Facebook"), [Amazon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amazon_(website) "Amazon (website)"), and [Reddit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reddit "Reddit")â€”all of them American-owned.[[560]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-alexa-topsitesus-583)

In 2025, the U.S. was the world's [second-largest video game market by revenue](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_video_games_markets_by_country "List of video games markets by country") (after China).[[561]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-584) In 2015, the U.S. video game industry consisted of 2,457 companies that employed around 220,000 jobs and generated $30.4 billion in revenue.[[562]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-:0-585) There are 444 game publishers, developers, and hardware companies in California alone.[[563]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-586) According to the [Game Developers Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Game_Developers_Conference "Game Developers Conference") (GDC), the U.S. is the top location for [video game development](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Video_game_development "Video game development"), with 58% of the world's [game developers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Video_game_developer "Video game developer") based there in 2025.[[564]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-587)

### Theater

Main article: [Theater in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theater_in_the_United_States "Theater in the United States")

[![Image 65](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Various_Pictures_from_New_York_City_-_September%2C_2025.jpg/250px-Various_Pictures_from_New_York_City_-_September%2C_2025.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Various_Pictures_from_New_York_City_-_September,_2025.jpg)

[Broadway theaters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Broadway_theater "Broadway theater") in [Theater District, Manhattan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theater_District,_Manhattan "Theater District, Manhattan")

The United States is well known for its theater. Mainstream theater in the United States derives from the old European theatrical tradition and has been heavily influenced by the [British theater](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theatre_of_the_United_Kingdom "Theatre of the United Kingdom").[[565]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Saxon2011-588) By the middle of the 19th century, America had created new distinct dramatic forms in the [Tom Shows](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tom_Shows "Tom Shows"), the [showboat theater](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Showboat "Showboat") and the [minstrel show](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minstrel_show "Minstrel show").[[566]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-589) The central hub of the American theater scene is the [Theater District in Manhattan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theater_District,_Manhattan "Theater District, Manhattan"), with its divisions of [Broadway](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Broadway_theatre "Broadway theatre"), [off-Broadway](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Off-Broadway "Off-Broadway"), and [off-off-Broadway](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Off-off-Broadway "Off-off-Broadway").[[567]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Londr%C3%A9Watermeier1998-590)

Many movie and television [celebrities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celebrity "Celebrity") have gotten their big break working in New York productions. Outside New York City, many cities have professional [regional or resident theater companies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regional_theater_in_the_United_States "Regional theater in the United States") that produce their own seasons. The biggest-budget theatrical productions are musicals. U.S. theater has an active [community theater](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Community_theater "Community theater") culture.[[568]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-591)

The [Tony Awards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tony_Awards "Tony Awards") recognizes excellence in live Broadway theater and are presented at an annual ceremony in [Manhattan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manhattan "Manhattan"). The awards are given for Broadway productions and performances. One is also given for [regional theater](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regional_theatre_in_the_United_States "Regional theatre in the United States"). Several discretionary non-competitive awards are given as well, including a [Special Tony Award](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special_Tony_Award "Special Tony Award"), the [Tony Honors for Excellence in Theatre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tony_Honors_for_Excellence_in_Theatre "Tony Honors for Excellence in Theatre"), and the [Isabelle Stevenson Award](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isabelle_Stevenson_Award "Isabelle Stevenson Award").[[569]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-592)

### Visual arts

Main articles: [Visual art of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visual_art_of_the_United_States "Visual art of the United States") and [Architecture of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Architecture_of_the_United_States "Architecture of the United States")

[![Image 66](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Grant_Wood_-_American_Gothic_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/250px-Grant_Wood_-_American_Gothic_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Grant_Wood_-_American_Gothic_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg)

_[American Gothic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American\_Gothic "American Gothic")_ (1930) by [Grant Wood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grant_Wood "Grant Wood") is one of the most famous [American paintings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visual_art_of_the_United_States "Visual art of the United States") and is widely [parodied](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parody "Parody").[[570]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-BBC-593)

[Folk art](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Folk_art_of_the_United_States "Folk art of the United States") in [colonial America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonial_america "Colonial america") grew out of artisanal [craftsmanship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Workmanship "Workmanship") in communities that allowed commonly trained people to individually express themselves. It was distinct from Europe's tradition of [high art](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High_culture "High culture"), which was less accessible and generally less relevant to early American settlers.[[571]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-594) Cultural movements in art and craftsmanship in colonial America generally lagged behind those of Western Europe. For example, the prevailing medieval style of [woodworking](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Woodworking "Woodworking") and primitive [sculpture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sculpture_of_the_United_States "Sculpture of the United States") became integral to early American folk art, despite the emergence of [Renaissance styles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Renaissance_art "Renaissance art") in England in the late 16th and early 17th centuries. The new English styles would have been early enough to make a considerable impact on American folk art, but American styles and forms had already been firmly adopted. Not only did styles change slowly in early America, but there was a tendency for rural artisans there to continue their traditional forms longer than their urban counterparts didâ€”and far longer than those in Western Europe.[[511]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Coleman-2013-534)

The [Hudson River School](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hudson_River_School "Hudson River School") was a mid-19th-century movement in the visual arts tradition of European [naturalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Realism_(arts) "Realism (arts)"). The 1913 [Armory Show](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armory_Show "Armory Show") in New York City, an exhibition of European [modernist art](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_art "Modern art"), shocked the public and transformed the U.S. art scene.[[572]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-595)

[American Realism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Realism "American Realism") and [American Regionalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Regionalism "American Regionalism") sought to reflect and give America new ways of looking at itself. [Georgia O'Keeffe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgia_O%27Keeffe "Georgia O'Keeffe"), [Marsden Hartley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marsden_Hartley "Marsden Hartley"), and others experimented with new and individualistic styles, which would become known as [American modernism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_modernism "American modernism"). Major artistic movements such as the [abstract expressionism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abstract_expressionism "Abstract expressionism") of [Jackson Pollock](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jackson_Pollock "Jackson Pollock") and [Willem de Kooning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Willem_de_Kooning "Willem de Kooning") and the [pop art](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pop_art "Pop art") of [Andy Warhol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andy_Warhol "Andy Warhol") and [Roy Lichtenstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roy_Lichtenstein "Roy Lichtenstein") developed largely in the United States. Major photographers include [Alfred Stieglitz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfred_Stieglitz "Alfred Stieglitz"), [Edward Steichen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Steichen "Edward Steichen"), [Dorothea Lange](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dorothea_Lange "Dorothea Lange"), [Edward Weston](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Weston "Edward Weston"), [James Van Der Zee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Van_Der_Zee "James Van Der Zee"), [Ansel Adams](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ansel_Adams "Ansel Adams"), and [Gordon Parks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gordon_Parks "Gordon Parks").[[573]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Davenport1991-596)

The tide of [modernism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modernism "Modernism") and then [postmodernism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Postmodernism "Postmodernism") has brought global fame to American architects, including [Frank Lloyd Wright](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Lloyd_Wright "Frank Lloyd Wright"), [Philip Johnson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philip_Johnson "Philip Johnson"), and [Frank Gehry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Gehry "Frank Gehry").[[574]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-JansonJanson2003-597) The [Metropolitan Museum of Art](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art "Metropolitan Museum of Art") in [Manhattan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manhattan "Manhattan") is the largest [art museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Art_museum "Art museum") in the United States[[575]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-METLargestArtMuseum-598) and the [fourth-largest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_largest_art_museums "List of largest art museums") in the world.[[576]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-599)

### Music

Main article: [Music of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Music_of_the_United_States "Music of the United States")

[![Image 67](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Country_Music_Hall_of_Fame_2022a.jpg/250px-Country_Music_Hall_of_Fame_2022a.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Country_Music_Hall_of_Fame_2022a.jpg)

The [Country Music Hall of Fame and Museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Country_Music_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum "Country Music Hall of Fame and Museum") in [Nashville, Tennessee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nashville,_Tennessee "Nashville, Tennessee")

[American folk music](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_folk_music "American folk music") encompasses numerous music genres, variously known as traditional music, traditional [folk music](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Folk_music "Folk music"), contemporary folk music, or roots music. Many traditional songs have been sung within the same family or folk group for generations, and sometimes trace back to such origins as the [British Isles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Isles "British Isles"), [mainland Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mainland_Europe "Mainland Europe"), or [Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/African-American_music "African-American music").[[577]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-afc-600) The rhythmic and lyrical styles of African-American music in particular have influenced American music.[[578]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-601)[Banjos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banjo "Banjo") were brought to America through the slave trade. [Minstrel shows](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minstrel_show "Minstrel show") incorporating the instrument into their acts led to its increased popularity and widespread production in the 19th century.[[579]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-602)[[580]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShi2016378-603) The [electric guitar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electric_guitar "Electric guitar"), first invented in the 1930s, and mass-produced by the 1940s, had an enormous influence on popular music, in particular due to the development of [rock and roll](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rock_and_roll "Rock and roll").[[581]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-axe-604) The [synthesizer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synthesizer "Synthesizer"), [turntablism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turntablism "Turntablism"), and [electronic music](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electronic_music "Electronic music") were also largely developed in the U.S.

Elements from folk idioms such as the [blues](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blues "Blues") and [old-time music](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old-time_music "Old-time music") were adopted and transformed into [popular genres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Popular_music "Popular music") with global audiences. [Jazz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jazz "Jazz") grew from blues and [ragtime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ragtime "Ragtime") in the early 20th century, developing from the innovations and recordings of composers such as [W.C. Handy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/W.C._Handy "W.C. Handy") and [Jelly Roll Morton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jelly_Roll_Morton "Jelly Roll Morton"). [Louis Armstrong](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_Armstrong "Louis Armstrong") and [Duke Ellington](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duke_Ellington "Duke Ellington") increased its popularity early in the 20th century.[[582]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Biddle-2001-605)[Country music](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Country_music "Country music") developed in the 1920s,[[583]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-606)[bluegrass](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bluegrass_music "Bluegrass music")[[584]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-607) and [rhythm and blues](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues "Rhythm and blues") in the 1940s,[[585]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOpenStax2014%C2%A7_[httpsopenstaxorgbooksus-historypages28-4-popular-culture-and-mass-media_28.4]-608) and rock and roll in the 1950s.[[581]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-axe-604) In the 1960s, [Bob Dylan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bob_Dylan "Bob Dylan") emerged from the [folk revival](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_folk_music_revival "American folk music revival") to become one of the country's most celebrated songwriters.[[586]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-609) The musical forms of [punk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Punk_rock "Punk rock") and [hip hop](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hip_hop "Hip hop") both originated in the United States in the 1970s.[[587]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-610)

The United States has the world's [largest music market](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_largest_recorded_music_markets "List of largest recorded music markets"), with a total retail value of $15.9 billion in 2022.[[588]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-611) Most of the world's [major record companies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Record_label#Major_labels "Record label") are based in the U.S.; they are represented by the [Recording Industry Association of America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America "Recording Industry Association of America") (RIAA).[[589]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-612) Mid-20th-century American pop stars, such as [Frank Sinatra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Sinatra "Frank Sinatra")[[590]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-613) and [Elvis Presley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elvis_Presley "Elvis Presley"),[[591]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-614) became [global celebrities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superstar "Superstar") and [best-selling music artists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists "List of best-selling music artists"),[[582]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Biddle-2001-605) as have artists of the late 20th century, such as [Michael Jackson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Jackson "Michael Jackson"),[[592]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-RIAA-615)[Madonna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madonna "Madonna"),[[593]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-616)[Whitney Houston](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Whitney_Houston "Whitney Houston"),[[594]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Rolling_Stone-2023-617) and [Mariah Carey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mariah_Carey "Mariah Carey"),[[595]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-618) and of the early 21st century, such as [Eminem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eminem "Eminem"),[[596]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-619)[Britney Spears](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Britney_Spears "Britney Spears"),[[597]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEdmondson2013490-620)[Lady Gaga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lady_Gaga "Lady Gaga"),[[597]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEdmondson2013490-620)[Katy Perry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Katy_Perry "Katy Perry"),[[597]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEdmondson2013490-620)[Taylor Swift](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taylor_Swift "Taylor Swift") and [BeyoncÃ©](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9 "BeyoncÃ©").[[598]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-621)

### Fashion

Main article: [Fashion in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fashion_in_the_United_States "Fashion in the United States")

[![Image 68](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Carolina_Herrera_AW14_12.jpg/250px-Carolina_Herrera_AW14_12.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Carolina_Herrera_AW14_12.jpg)

_[Haute couture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haute\_couture "Haute couture")_[fashion models](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fashion_model "Fashion model") on the [catwalk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catwalk "Catwalk") during [New York Fashion Week](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Fashion_Week "New York Fashion Week")

The United States has the world's largest [apparel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apparel "Apparel") market by revenue.[[599]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-622) Apart from professional [business attire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Business_attire "Business attire"), American fashion is eclectic and predominantly informal. Americans' diverse cultural roots are reflected in their clothing; however, [sneakers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sneaker "Sneaker"), [jeans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeans "Jeans"), [T-shirts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/T-shirts "T-shirts"), and [baseball caps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baseball_cap "Baseball cap") are emblematic of American styles.[[600]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-AmericanClassicFashion-623) New York, with [its Fashion Week](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Fashion_Week "New York Fashion Week"), is considered to be one of the "Big Four" global [fashion capitals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fashion_capital "Fashion capital"), along with [Paris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris_Fashion_Week "Paris Fashion Week"), [Milan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milan_Fashion_Week "Milan Fashion Week"), and [London](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/London_Fashion_Week "London Fashion Week"). A study demonstrated that general proximity to [Manhattan's Garment District](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Garment_District,_Manhattan "Garment District, Manhattan") has been synonymous with American fashion since its inception in the early 20th century.[[601]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-GarmentDistrictNYCFashionSymbolUS-624)

A number of well-known [designer labels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Designer_label "Designer label"), among them [Tommy Hilfiger](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tommy_Hilfiger_(company) "Tommy Hilfiger (company)"), [Ralph Lauren](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ralph_Lauren_Corporation "Ralph Lauren Corporation"), [Tom Ford](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tom_Ford_(brand) "Tom Ford (brand)") and [Calvin Klein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calvin_Klein_(fashion_house) "Calvin Klein (fashion house)"), are headquartered in [Manhattan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manhattan "Manhattan").[[602]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-625)[[603]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-626) Labels cater to [niche markets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Niche_market "Niche market"), such as preteens. [New York Fashion Week](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Fashion_Week "New York Fashion Week") is one of the most influential fashion shows in the world, and is held twice each year in Manhattan;[[604]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-USNYCFashionWeekGlobalIndustryTonesetter-627) the annual [Met Gala](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Met_Gala "Met Gala"), also in Manhattan, has been called the fashion world's "biggest night".[[605]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-MetGalaFashion'sBiggestNight1-628)[[606]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-MetGalaFashion'sBiggestNight2-629)

### Cinema

Main article: [Cinema of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cinema_of_the_United_States "Cinema of the United States")

[![Image 69](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hollywood_Sign_%28Zuschnitt%29.jpg/250px-Hollywood_Sign_%28Zuschnitt%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Hollywood_Sign_(Zuschnitt).jpg)

The [Hollywood Sign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hollywood_Sign "Hollywood Sign") in the [Hollywood Hills](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hollywood_Hills "Hollywood Hills"), often regarded as the symbol of the [American film industry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_film_industry "American film industry")

The U.S. film industry has [a worldwide influence and following](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Hollywood "Global Hollywood"). [Hollywood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hollywood,_Los_Angeles "Hollywood, Los Angeles"), a district in northern Los Angeles, the nation's second-most populous city, is also [metonymous](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metonymous "Metonymous") for the American filmmaking industry.[[607]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-630)[[608]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-631)[[609]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-632) The [major film studios](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Major_film_studios "Major film studios") of the United States are the primary source of the [most commercially successful](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films "List of highest-grossing films") movies selling the most tickets in the world.[[610]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Kerrigan_Page_18-633)[[611]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Davis-634)

Largely centered in the New York City region from its beginnings in the late 19th century through the first decades of the 20th century,[[612]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-635)[[613]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-636)[[614]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-637)[[615]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-638) the U.S. film industry has since been primarily based in and around Hollywood. Nonetheless, American film companies have been subject to the forces of [globalization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Globalization "Globalization") in the 21st century, and an increasing number of films are made elsewhere.[[616]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-639) The [Academy Awards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_Awards "Academy Awards"), popularly known as "the Oscars", have been held annually by the [Academy of Motion Picture Arts and Sciences](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_of_Motion_Picture_Arts_and_Sciences "Academy of Motion Picture Arts and Sciences") since 1929,[[617]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-DrowneHuber2004-640) and the [Golden Globe Awards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award "Golden Globe Award") have been held annually since January 1944.[[618]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Kroon2014-641)

The industry peaked in what is commonly referred to as the "[Golden Age of Hollywood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Classical_Hollywood_cinema "Classical Hollywood cinema")", from the early sound period until the early 1960s,[[619]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-642) with screen actors such as [John Wayne](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Wayne "John Wayne") and [Marilyn Monroe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marilyn_Monroe "Marilyn Monroe") becoming iconic figures.[[620]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-643)[[621]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-644) In the 1970s, "[New Hollywood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Hollywood "New Hollywood")", or the "Hollywood Renaissance",[[622]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Greven2013-645) was defined by grittier films influenced by French and Italian realist pictures of the [post-war period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aftermath_of_World_War_II "Aftermath of World War II").[[623]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Morrison1998-646) The 21st century has been marked by the rise of American [streaming platforms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Streaming_platform "Streaming platform"), which came to rival traditional cinema.[[624]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-RE-647)[[625]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-648)

### Cuisine

Main article: [American cuisine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_cuisine "American cuisine")

[![Image 70](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/2019-11-28_14_46_15_A_single_serving_of_Thanksgiving_Dinner_in_the_Parkway_Village_section_of_Ewing_Township%2C_Mercer_County%2C_New_Jersey.jpg/250px-2019-11-28_14_46_15_A_single_serving_of_Thanksgiving_Dinner_in_the_Parkway_Village_section_of_Ewing_Township%2C_Mercer_County%2C_New_Jersey.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:2019-11-28_14_46_15_A_single_serving_of_Thanksgiving_Dinner_in_the_Parkway_Village_section_of_Ewing_Township,_Mercer_County,_New_Jersey.jpg)

A [Thanksgiving dinner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thanksgiving_dinner "Thanksgiving dinner") with [roast turkey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roast_turkey "Roast turkey"), [mashed potatoes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mashed_potatoes "Mashed potatoes"), [pickles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pickled_cucumber "Pickled cucumber"), [corn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corn "Corn"), [candied yams](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Candied_yams "Candied yams"), [cranberry jelly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cranberry_jelly "Cranberry jelly"), [shrimps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shrimp_and_prawn_as_food "Shrimp and prawn as food"), [stuffing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stuffing "Stuffing"), [green peas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_peas "Green peas"), [deviled eggs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deviled_eggs "Deviled eggs"), [green salad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_salad "Green salad"), and [apple sauce](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_sauce "Apple sauce")

Early settlers were introduced by Native Americans to foods such as [turkey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey_as_food "Turkey as food"), [sweet potatoes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sweet_potato "Sweet potato"), [corn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maize "Maize"), [squash](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cucurbita "Cucurbita"), and [maple syrup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maple_syrup "Maple syrup"). Of the most enduring and pervasive examples are variations of the native dish called [succotash](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Succotash "Succotash"). Early settlers and later immigrants combined these with foods they were familiar with, such as [wheat flour](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wheat_flour "Wheat flour"),[[626]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Wheat-649) beef, and milk, to create a distinctive American cuisine.[[627]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-650)[[628]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-651)[New World crops](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_World_crops "New World crops"), especially [pumpkin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pumpkin "Pumpkin"), corn, [potatoes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Potatoes "Potatoes"), and turkey as the main course are part of a shared national menu on [Thanksgiving](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thanksgiving_(United_States) "Thanksgiving (United States)"), when many Americans prepare or purchase traditional dishes to celebrate the occasion.[[629]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Mintz1996-652)

Characteristic American dishes such as [apple pie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_pie "Apple pie"), [fried chicken](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fried_chicken "Fried chicken"), [doughnuts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doughnut "Doughnut"), [french fries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_fries "French fries"), [macaroni and cheese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macaroni_and_cheese "Macaroni and cheese"), [ice cream](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ice_cream "Ice cream"), [hamburgers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamburger "Hamburger"), [hot dogs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hot_dog "Hot dog"), and [American pizza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pizza_in_the_United_States "Pizza in the United States") derive from the recipes of various immigrant groups.[[630]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-653)[[631]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-654)[[632]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-655)[[633]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-656)[Mexican dishes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexican-American_cuisine "Mexican-American cuisine") such as [burritos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burritos "Burritos") and [tacos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tacos "Tacos") preexisted the United States in areas later annexed from Mexico, and [adaptations of Chinese cuisine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Chinese_cuisine "American Chinese cuisine") as well as [pasta dishes freely adapted from Italian sources](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian-American_cuisine "Italian-American cuisine") are all widely consumed.[[634]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-IFT-657)

American [chefs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chef "Chef") have had a significant impact on society both domestically and internationally. In 1946, the [Culinary Institute of America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culinary_Institute_of_America "Culinary Institute of America") was founded by [Katharine Angell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Katharine_Cramer_Angell "Katharine Cramer Angell") and [Frances Roth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frances_Roth "Frances Roth"). This would become the United States' most prestigious culinary school, where many of the most talented American chefs would study prior to successful careers.[[635]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-658)[[636]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FTfbs-659) The [United States restaurant industry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_restaurant_industry "United States restaurant industry") was projected at $899 billion in sales for 2020,[[637]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Brownfield-2020-660)[[638]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Ramirez-661) and employed more than 15 million people, representing 10% of the nation's workforce directly.[[637]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Brownfield-2020-660) It is the country's second-largest private employer and the third-largest employer overall.[[639]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Noguchi-2020-662)[[640]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-663) The United States is home to over 220 [Michelin star](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michelin_star "Michelin star")-rated restaurants, 70 of which are in New York City alone.[[641]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-664)

[Wine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_wine "American wine") has been produced in what is now the United States since the 1500s, with the [first widespread production beginning in what is now New Mexico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Mexico_wine "New Mexico wine") in 1628.[[642]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-665)[[643]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Birchell_Steel_2013_p.-666)[[644]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-New_Mexico._Office_of_Cultural_Affairs_1995_p.-667) In the modern U.S., wine production is undertaken in all fifty states, with [California producing 84 percent of all U.S. wine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_wine "California wine"). With more than 1,100,000 acres (4,500 km 2) under vine, the United States is the [fourth-largest wine-producing country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_wine_production "List of countries by wine production") in the world, after [Italy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_wine "Italian wine"), [Spain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_wine "Spanish wine"), and [France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_wine "French wine").[[645]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Sotheby,_p._462-668)[[646]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Oxford,_p._719-669)

The [classic American diner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diner "Diner"), a casual restaurant type originally intended for the working class, emerged during the 19th century from converted railroad [dining cars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dining_car "Dining car") made stationary. The diner soon evolved into purpose-built structures whose number expanded greatly in the 20th century.[[647]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-670) The American [fast-food](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fast-food "Fast-food") industry developed alongside the nation's [car culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Car_culture "Car culture").[[648]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-671) American restaurants developed the [drive-in](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drive-in "Drive-in") format in the 1920s, which they began to replace with the [drive-through](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drive-through "Drive-through") format by the 1940s.[[649]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-drivethru-672)[[650]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-673) American [fast-food restaurant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fast-food_restaurant "Fast-food restaurant") chains, such as [McDonald's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/McDonald%27s "McDonald's"), [Burger King](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burger_King "Burger King"), [Chick-fil-A](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chick-fil-A "Chick-fil-A"), [Kentucky Fried Chicken](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kentucky_Fried_Chicken "Kentucky Fried Chicken"), [Dunkin' Donuts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dunkin%27_Donuts "Dunkin' Donuts") and [many others](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_fast_food_restaurant_chains#United_States "List of fast food restaurant chains"), have numerous outlets around the world.[[651]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-Pavlova-2019-674)

### Sports

Main articles: [Sports in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sports_in_the_United_States "Sports in the United States") and [United States at the Olympics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_at_the_Olympics "United States at the Olympics")

[![Image 71](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Delhomme_goes_deep.jpg/250px-Delhomme_goes_deep.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Delhomme_goes_deep.jpg)

[American football](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_football "American football") is the most popular sport in the United States; in this 2009 [National Football League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Football_League "National Football League") game, [Carolina Panthers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carolina_Panthers "Carolina Panthers") quarterback [Jake Delhomme](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jake_Delhomme "Jake Delhomme") (number 17) throws a forward pass against the [Dallas Cowboys](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dallas_Cowboys "Dallas Cowboys").

The most popular spectator sports in the U.S. are [American football](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_football_in_the_United_States "American football in the United States"), [basketball](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basketball_in_the_United_States "Basketball in the United States"), [baseball](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baseball_in_the_United_States "Baseball in the United States"), [soccer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soccer_in_the_United_States "Soccer in the United States"), and [ice hockey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ice_hockey_in_the_United_States "Ice hockey in the United States").[[652]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-675) While most major U.S. sports such as baseball and American football have evolved out of European practices, basketball, [volleyball](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volleyball_in_the_United_States "Volleyball in the United States"), [skateboarding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Skateboarding "Skateboarding"), and [snowboarding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Snowboarding "Snowboarding") are American inventions, many of which have become popular worldwide.[[653]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-676)[Lacrosse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lacrosse_in_the_United_States "Lacrosse in the United States") and [surfing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surfing_in_the_United_States "Surfing in the United States") arose from Native American and Native Hawaiian activities that predate European contact.[[654]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-liss-677) The [market for professional sports in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Professional_sports_market_in_the_United_States "Professional sports market in the United States") was approximately $69 billion in July 2013, roughly 50% larger than that of Europe, the Middle East, and Africa combined.[[655]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-678)

American football is by several measures the most popular spectator sport in the United States;[[656]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-679) the [National Football League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Football_League "National Football League") has the highest average attendance of any sports league in the world, and the [Super Bowl](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Super_Bowl "Super Bowl") is watched by tens of millions globally.[[657]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-680) However, baseball has been regarded as the U.S. "[national sport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_sport "National sport")" since the late 19th century. After American football, the next four most popular professional team sports are basketball, baseball, soccer, and ice hockey. Their premier leagues are, respectively, the [National Basketball Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Basketball_Association "National Basketball Association"),[[658]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-681)[Major League Baseball](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Major_League_Baseball "Major League Baseball"),[[659]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-682)[Major League Soccer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Major_League_Soccer "Major League Soccer"),[[660]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-683) and the [National Hockey League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Hockey_League "National Hockey League").[[661]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-684) The most-watched [individual sports](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Individual_sport "Individual sport") in the U.S. are [golf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golf_in_the_United_States "Golf in the United States") and [auto racing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auto_racing "Auto racing"), particularly [NASCAR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NASCAR "NASCAR") and [IndyCar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IndyCar "IndyCar").[[662]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-685)[[663]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-686)

On the [collegiate level](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/College_athletics_in_the_United_States "College athletics in the United States"), earnings for the member institutions exceed $1 billion annually,[[664]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-si-687) and [college football](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/College_football "College football") and [basketball](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/College_basketball "College basketball") attract large audiences, as the [NCAA March Madness tournament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_men%27s_basketball_tournament "NCAA Division I men's basketball tournament") and the [College Football Playoff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/College_Football_Playoff "College Football Playoff") are some of the most watched national sporting events.[[665]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-688) In the U.S., the intercollegiate sports level serves as the main feeder system for professional and Olympic sports, with significant exceptions such as [Minor League Baseball](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minor_League_Baseball "Minor League Baseball"). This differs greatly from practices in nearly all other countries, where publicly and privately funded sports organizations serve this function.[[666]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-689)

Eight [Olympic Games](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olympic_Games "Olympic Games") have taken place in the United States. The [1904 Summer Olympics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1904_Summer_Olympics "1904 Summer Olympics") in [St. Louis, Missouri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St._Louis,_Missouri "St. Louis, Missouri"), were the first-ever Olympic Games held outside of Europe.[[667]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-690) The Olympic Games will be held in the U.S. for a ninth time when Los Angeles hosts the [2028 Summer Olympics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2028_Summer_Olympics "2028 Summer Olympics"). [U.S. athletes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_at_the_Olympics "United States at the Olympics") have won a total of 2,968 medals (1,179 gold) at the Olympic Games, the most of any country.[[668]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-691)[[669]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-692)[[670]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-693)

In other international competition, the United States is the home of a number of prestigious events, including the [Americas Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Americas_Cup "Americas Cup"), [World Baseball Classic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Baseball_Classic "World Baseball Classic"), the [U.S. Open](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Open_(tennis) "U.S. Open (tennis)"), and the [Masters Tournament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masters_Tournament "Masters Tournament"). The [U.S. men's national soccer team](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team "United States men's national soccer team") has qualified for [eleven World Cups](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_at_the_FIFA_World_Cup "United States at the FIFA World Cup"), while the [women's national team](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_women%27s_national_soccer_team "United States women's national soccer team") has [won](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_at_the_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup "United States at the FIFA Women's World Cup") the [FIFA Women's World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup "FIFA Women's World Cup") and [Olympic soccer tournament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Football_at_the_Summer_Olympics "Football at the Summer Olympics") four times each.[[671]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-694) The [1999 FIFA Women's World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1999_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup "1999 FIFA Women's World Cup") was hosted by the United States. [Its final match](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1999_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup_final "1999 FIFA Women's World Cup final") was attended by 90,185, setting the world record for largest women's sporting event crowd at the time.[[672]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-695) The United States hosted the [1994 FIFA World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup "1994 FIFA World Cup") and will co-host, along with Canada and Mexico, the [2026 FIFA World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_FIFA_World_Cup "2026 FIFA World Cup").[[673]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-696)

3.   ^ [Jump up to: _**a**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_ref-largestcountry_15-0)[_**b**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_ref-largestcountry_15-1)[_**c**_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_ref-largestcountry_15-2)At 3,531,900 sq mi (9,147,590 km 2), the United States is the third-largest country in the world by land area, behind [Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia "Russia") and [China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China "China"). By total area (land and water), it is the third-largest, behind Russia and [Canada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canada "Canada"), if its coastal and territorial water areas are included. However, if only its internal waters are included (bays, sounds, rivers, lakes, and the [Great Lakes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Lakes "Great Lakes")), the U.S. is the fourth-largest, after Russia, Canada, and China. 

 Coastal/territorial waters included: 3,796,742 sq mi (9,833,517 km 2)[[20]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-CIA_Factbook_Area-30)

 Only internal waters included: 3,696,100 sq mi (9,572,900 km 2)[[21]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-31)

10.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_ref-29 "Jump up")**The five major territories outside the union of states are [American Samoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Samoa "American Samoa"), [Guam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guam "Guam"), the [Northern Mariana Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands "Northern Mariana Islands"), [Puerto Rico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puerto_Rico "Puerto Rico"), and the [U.S. Virgin Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands "United States Virgin Islands"). The seven undisputed island areas without permanent populations are [Baker Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baker_Island "Baker Island"), [Howland Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Howland_Island "Howland Island"), [Jarvis Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jarvis_Island "Jarvis Island"), [Johnston Atoll](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johnston_Atoll "Johnston Atoll"), [Kingman Reef](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingman_Reef "Kingman Reef"), [Midway Atoll](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Midway_Atoll "Midway Atoll"), and [Palmyra Atoll](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palmyra_Atoll "Palmyra Atoll"). U.S. sovereignty over the unpopulated [Bajo Nuevo Bank](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bajo_Nuevo_Bank "Bajo Nuevo Bank"), [Navassa Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Navassa_Island "Navassa Island"), [Serranilla Bank](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serranilla_Bank "Serranilla Bank"), and [Wake Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wake_Island "Wake Island") is disputed.[[19]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-HRI-2012-28)
11.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_ref-pop_clock_32-0 "Jump up")**The [U.S. Census Bureau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau "United States Census Bureau")'s latest official population estimate of 340,110,988 residents (2024) is for the 50 states and the District of Columbia; it excludes the 3.6 million residents of the five major [U.S. territories](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States "Territories of the United States") and outlying islands. The Census Bureau also provides a continuously updated but unofficial population clock: [www.census.gov/popclock](https://www.census.gov/popclock/)
12.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_ref-38 "Jump up")**The official [U.S. Government Publishing Office Style Manual](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Government_Publishing_Office_Style_Manual "U.S. Government Publishing Office Style Manual") has prescribed specific usages for "U.S." and "United States" as part of official names. In "formal writing (treaties, Executive orders, proclamations, etc.); congressional bills; legal citations and courtwork; and covers and title pages",[[26]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-gpo-stylemanual-37) "United States" is always used. In a sentence containing the name of another country, "United States" must be used. Otherwise, "U.S." is used preceding a government organization or as an adjective, but "United States" is used as an adjective preceding non-governmental organizations (e.g. [United States Steel Corporation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Steel_Corporation "United States Steel Corporation")).[[26]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-gpo-stylemanual-37)

14.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_ref-43 "Jump up")**_Americus_ comes from the [Medieval Latin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medieval_Latin "Medieval Latin") name _Emericus_ (for [Saint Emeric of Hungary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saint_Emeric_of_Hungary "Saint Emeric of Hungary")), itself derived from the Old High German name [Emmerich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emmerich_(name) "Emmerich (name)").
15.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_ref-72 "Jump up")**From the late 15th century, the [Columbian exchange](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Columbian_exchange "Columbian exchange") had been catastrophic for native populations throughout the Americas. It is estimated [that up to 95 percent of the Indigenous populations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virgin_soil_epidemic "Virgin soil epidemic"), especially in the Caribbean, [perished from infectious diseases during the years following European colonization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Native_American_disease_and_epidemics "Native American disease and epidemics");[[55]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-69) remaining populations were often displaced by European expansion.[[56]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJoseph2016590-70)[[57]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-71)

20.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_ref-369 "Jump up")**A country's total exports are usually understood to be goods and services. Based on this, the U.S. is the world's second-largest exporter, after China.[[348]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-367) However, if primary income is included, the U.S. is the world's largest exporter.[[349]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_note-368)

22.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States#cite_ref-459 "Jump up")**[Inupiaq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inupiaq_language "Inupiaq language"), [Siberian Yupik](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Siberian_Yupik_language "Central Siberian Yupik language"), [Central Alaskan Yup'ik](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Alaskan_Yup%27ik_language "Central Alaskan Yup'ik language"), [Alutiiq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alutiiq_language "Alutiiq language"), [Unanga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aleut_language "Aleut language") (Aleut), [DenaÊ¼ina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dena%CA%BCina_language "DenaÊ¼ina language"), [Deg Xinag](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deg_Xinag_language "Deg Xinag language"), [Holikachuk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holikachuk_language "Holikachuk language"), [Koyukon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Koyukon_language "Koyukon language"), [Upper Kuskokwim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Upper_Kuskokwim_language "Upper Kuskokwim language"), [GwichÊ¼in](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gwich%CA%BCin_language "GwichÊ¼in language"), [Tanana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lower_Tanana_language "Lower Tanana language"), [Upper Tanana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Upper_Tanana_language "Upper Tanana language"), [Tanacross](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tanacross_language "Tanacross language"), [HÃ¤n](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H%C3%A4n_language "HÃ¤n language"), [Ahtna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahtna_language "Ahtna language"), [Eyak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eyak_language "Eyak language"), [Tlingit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tlingit_language "Tlingit language"), [Haida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haida_language "Haida language"), and [Tsimshian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coast_Tsimshian_dialect "Coast Tsimshian dialect")

As with the Beer Hall Putsch, a would-be leader tried to take advantage of an already scheduled event (in Hitler's case, Kahr's speech; in Trump's, Congress's tallying of the electoral votes) to create a dramatic moment with himself at the center of attention, calling for bold action to upend the political order. Unlike Hitler's coup attempt, Trump already held top of office, so he was attempting to hold onto power, not seize it (the precise term for Trump's intended action is a 'self-coup' or 'autogolpe'). Thus, Trump was able to plan for the event well in advance, and with much greater control, including developing the legal arguments that could be used to justify rejecting the election's results. (p. 3)
